Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
Research Gap: Dialectic in the Prophetic Sunnah
Author outlines four research topics: jadal in Sunnah, monographs, Greek influence, and manuscript studies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the research gap concerning dialectic in the Prophetic Sunnah and formulate a research question to address it.

Core Idea
The Sunnah's dialectic is an open field ready for exploration.

In this passage, the author notes that while Quranic dialectic has been thoroughly studied, no work exists on dialectic in the Sunnah. This lesson empowers you to recognize such gaps and kickstart new research.

Guided Path
1
Contrast existing and missing studies
The author states that studies on jadal in the Quran are abundant, but none exist for the Sunnah. Note this contrast – it highlights a clear gap.
2
Evaluate the importance of the gap
Why is studying jadal in the Sunnah important? The Sunnah is a primary source of legislation and contains numerous arguments and debates. Neglecting it means missing a crucial dimension of prophetic guidance.
3
Formulate a research question
Based on the gap, craft a specific question, e.g., 'What are the main features of dialectical argumentation in the Prophetic Sunnah and how do they relate to usuli jadal?'
Ensure your question is researchable and focused.
4
Outline a research plan
Briefly sketch the methodology: collect relevant hadiths, analyze argument patterns, compare with Quranic jadal, and derive implications for usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثانيا : آفاق البحث : إن هذا البحث ما هو في الحقيقة إلا بداية أو مفتاح لبحوث أخرى ظهرت معالمها إثر الانتهاء من دراسة هذا الموضوع ويمكن أن نؤشر هنا على بعض الموضوعات التي يمكن أن تتخذ مجالا للبحوث العلمية من قبل الباحثين مستقبلا : 1 - ظهرت مجموعة من الدراسات التي تناولت البحث في موضوع «الجدل في القرآن الكريم حيث أحاطت بالموضوع من جميع جوانبه تقريبا، لكن بالمقابل لم نقف على كتاب أو رسالة أو بحث متعلق بالجدل في السنة النبوية الشريفة، فهذا موضوع مهم جدا يكتسي أهمية بالغة، ويتطلب أن ينهض باحث أو مجموعة من الباحثين لدراسته من جوانبه المختلفة 2 - كتب علماء الأصول مجموعة من الكتب الخاصة بالجدل، وقد عرضنا للحديث عنها بصورة مختصرة جدا في الباب التمهيدي، وهذه الكتب تحتاج هي ذاتها إلى دراسات علمية خاصة بكل منها فيمكن لمجموعة من الباحثين أن يتناول كل منهم موضوعًا من الموضوعات الآتية مثلا : «الجدل عند إمام الحرمين» أو «الجدل عند الشيرازي» أو «الجدل عند الباجي» أو «الجدل عند ابن عقيل» أو الجدل عند الطوفي». 3 - معلوم أن اليونان كان عندهم منهج في الجدل وهذا المنهج انتقل إلى العالم الإسلامي عندما ترجم المسلمون كتب اليونان بداية من عصر المأمون الخليفة العباسي، فهل كانت للجدل الأصولي علاقة بالجدل اليوناني وهل تأثر الأصوليون المسلمون في كتاباتهم الجدلية بكتابات اليونانيين الجدلية، وخاصة منها مؤلفات أرسطو ؟ أم أن الأصوليين المسلمين لهم منهجهم المستقل الذي لا علاقة له بمنهج اليونان؟ إن هذا التساؤل جدير بالطرح، ويتطلب أن يقوم باحث أو مجموعة من الباحثين بدراسة هذا الموضوع ويمكن أن يتم تناوله تحت عنوان علاقة الجدل الأصولي بالجدل الأرسطي أو اليوناني»، بحيث يكون البحث مقارنا بين المنهجين . 4 - هناك العديد من كتب الأصوليين في الجدل لا تزال مخطوطة وبعيدة عن أن تتناولها أيدي الباحثين المهتمين، وهذا يتطلب أن يتجرد مجموعة من طلاب العلم والباحثين في الدراسات العليا الشرعية للبحث عن هذه المخطوطات في مظانها ومحاولة الحصول عليها بنسخها المتعددة - إن وجدت - ثم دراستها دراسة علمية، بحيث يتم تسجيلها كرسائل جامعية للحصول على الماجستير أو الدكتوراه في شكل تحقيق ودراسة، ويمكن أن نشير هنا مثلا إلى كتاب «المنتحل في الجدل» لأبي حامد الغزالي، المنقذ من الذلل في مسائل الجدل» لعبد العزيز النسفي والجدل والكاشف عن أصول الدلائل وفصول العلل»، لفخر الدين الرازي، ومنهاج العمل في صناعة الجدل لأبي عبد الله اللآردي، و«كتاب المناظرات في الأسئلة والاعتراضات على أنواع الاستدلالات» لابن المعمار
Second: Research Horizons: This research is in reality only a beginning or a key to other researches whose features have appeared after completing the study of this topic. We can point here to some topics that can become fields for scientific research by researchers in the future: 1 - A group of studies have emerged that dealt with research on the topic of 'Dialectic in the Holy Quran' and covered the topic from almost all its aspects, but on the other hand we have not come across a book, thesis, or research related to dialectic in the noble Prophetic Sunnah. This is a very important topic of great significance, and it requires that a researcher or a group of researchers undertake to study it from its various aspects. 2 - The scholars of usul have authored a group of books specifically on dialectic, and we have discussed them very briefly in the introductory chapter. These books themselves need specific scientific studies for each one. Thus a group of researchers can each take one of the following topics, for example: 'Dialectic according to Imam al-Haramayn' or 'Dialectic according to al-Shirazi' or 'Dialectic according to al-Baji' or 'Dialectic according to Ibn Aqil' or 'Dialectic according to al-Tufi'. 3 - It is known that the Greeks had a method in dialectic, and this method was transmitted to the Islamic world when the Muslims translated the books of the Greeks starting from the era of the Caliph al-Ma'mun. So, was there a relationship between usuli dialectic and Greek dialectic? Were Muslim usul scholars influenced in their dialectical writings by the dialectical writings of the Greeks, especially Aristotle's works? Or do Muslim usul scholars have their own independent method that has no relation to the Greek method? This question is worthy of being raised, and it requires that a researcher or a group of researchers study this topic. It can be addressed under the title 'The Relationship of Usuli Dialectic to Aristotelian or Greek Dialectic', such that the research is comparative between the two methods. 4 - There are many books by usul scholars on dialectic that are still manuscripts and far from being reached by the hands of interested researchers. This requires that a group of students of knowledge and researchers in higher Islamic studies devote themselves to searching for these manuscripts in their locations and attempting to obtain them in their multiple copies - if they exist - then studying them scientifically, so that they are registered as university theses for Master's or Doctorate in the form of critical edition and study. We can point here, for example, to the book 'al-Muntahal fi al-Jadal' by Abu Hamid al-Ghazali, 'al-Munqidh min al-Dalal fi Masa'il al-Jadal' by Abd al-Aziz al-Nasafi, 'al-Jadal wa al-Kashif 'an Usul al-Dala'il wa Fusul al-'Ilal' by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, 'Minhaj al-Amal fi Sina'at al-Jadal' by Abu Abd Allah al-Lardi, and 'Kitab al-Munazarat fi al-As'ila wa al-I'tiradat 'ala Anwa' al-Istidlalat' by Ibn al-Mi'mar.
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage concludes the book or chapter by offering suggestions for future research in usuli dialectic. It is a forward-looking section, not a logical argument but a call to action. The author identifies four main areas: First, while dialectic in the Quran has been well-studied, dialectic in the Sunnah remains neglected and deserves comprehensive research. Second, the many specialized books on jadal by usul scholars (e.g., by Imam al-Haramayn, al-Shirazi, al-Baji, Ibn Aqil, al-Tufi) each require individual monographic studies. Third, the historical question of Greek influence on Islamic dialectic is posed: did Muslim usul scholars borrow from Aristotle and other Greeks, or did they develop an independent method? A comparative study is suggested. Fourth, many important manuscripts on jadal are still unpublished and need critical editions for graduate theses; specific examples are given, including works by al-Ghazali, al-Nasafi, al-Razi, al-Lardi, and Ibn al-Mi'mar. Each point is a direct recommendation, and the author provides concrete examples to guide future researchers.

Key Terms
الجدل في السنة النبوية
فجوة البحث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which statement is true about research on dialectic?
A) Dialectic in the Quran has been thoroughly studied.
B) Dialectic in the Sunnah has been studied more than in the Quran.
C) No research exists on dialectic in the Quran.
D) Dialectic in the Sunnah is equally well-studied.

Key Takeaway
Identifying untapped research areas is a crucial skill for advancing usul al-fiqh and Islamic logic.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the author's observation, write a one-paragraph research proposal for studying dialectic in the Prophetic Sunnah, including a potential title and methodology.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
Monographic Studies on Usuli Jadal Scholars
Author outlines four research topics: jadal in Sunnah, monographs, Greek influence, and manuscript studies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key usuli scholars who wrote on jadal and argue why each deserves a dedicated monograph.

Core Idea
Each major usuli scholar's jadal work is a unique intellectual monument waiting to be excavated.

The author lists several scholars whose specialized jadal books need individual study. This lesson guides you in understanding the value of focused monographs on these figures.

Guided Path
1
List the scholars mentioned
The author names Imam al-Haramayn, al-Shirazi, al-Baji, Ibn Aqil, and al-Tufi. Write down their names and recall their contributions to usul al-fiqh.
2
Research their jadal works
For each, find the title of their jadal book (if known) and its content scope. For example, al-Shirazi's al-Ma'una fi al-Jadal.
Use library catalogues or digital resources.
3
Justify a monograph study
Explain why a full monograph on, say, 'Jadal according to al-Baji' would be valuable: it would reveal his argumentation style, his responses to opponents, and his influence on later usul.
Consider the historical context and available sources.
4
Formulate a research outline
Draft a possible chapter structure: biography, methodology, comparison with contemporaries, evaluation.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
Greek Influence on Usuli Dialectic: A Comparative Inquiry
Author outlines four research topics: jadal in Sunnah, monographs, Greek influence, and manuscript studies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to formulate a comparative research question regarding the relationship between usuli and Greek dialectic and outline a comparative study.

Core Idea
The unresolved question of Greek influence on Islamic jadal is a fascinating comparative project.

The author raises a critical historical question: Did usuli scholars borrow from Greek dialectic or develop their own independent method? This lesson helps you design a comparative research project to answer it.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two hypotheses
Hypothesis A: Usuli jadal was influenced by Greek (Aristotelian) dialectic. Hypothesis B: It was developed independently. Grasp the implications of each.
2
Identify primary sources
List key Greek texts (e.g., Aristotle's Topics) and key usuli jadal works (e.g., those by al-Shirazi, al-Ghazali).
Consider the translation movement under al-Ma'mun.
3
Establish comparison criteria
Decide on aspects to compare: terminology, structure of debate, types of arguments, goals of dialectic.
4
Create a comparative analysis plan
Draft a chapter outline: introduction to both traditions, point-by-point comparison, evaluation of influence vs. independence.
The author suggests the title: 'The Relationship of Usuli Dialectic to Aristotelian or Greek Dialectic'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

معلوم أن اليونان كان عندهم منهج في الجدل وهذا المنهج انتقل إلى العالم الإسلامي عندما ترجم المسلمون كتب اليونان بداية من عصر المأمون الخليفة العباسي، فهل كانت للجدل الأصولي علاقة بالجدل اليوناني وهل تأثر الأصوليون المسلمون في كتاباتهم الجدلية بكتابات اليونانيين الجدلية، وخاصة منها مؤلفات أرسطو ؟ أم أن الأصوليين المسلمين لهم منهجهم المستقل الذي لا علاقة له بمنهج اليونان؟ إن هذا التساؤل جدير بالطرح، ويتطلب أن يقوم باحث أو مجموعة من الباحثين بدراسة هذا الموضوع ويمكن أن يتم تناوله تحت عنوان علاقة الجدل الأصولي بالجدل الأرسطي أو اليوناني»، بحيث يكون البحث مقارنا بين المنهجين . 4 - هناك العديد من كتب الأصوليين في الجدل لا تزال مخطوطة وبعيدة عن أن تتناولها أيدي الباحثين المهتمين، وهذا يتطلب أن يتجرد مجموعة من طلاب العلم والباحثين في الدراسات العليا الشرعية للبحث عن هذه المخطوطات في مظانها ومحاولة الحصول عليها بنسخها المتعددة - إن وجدت - ثم دراستها دراسة علمية، بحيث يتم تسجيلها كرسائل جامعية للحصول على الماجستير أو الدكتوراه في شكل تحقيق ودراسة، ويمكن أن نشير هنا مثلا إلى كتاب «المنتحل في الجدل» لأبي حامد الغزالي، المنقذ من الذلل في مسائل الجدل» لعبد العزيز النسفي والجدل والكاشف عن أصول الدلائل وفصول العلل»، لفخر الدين الرازي، ومنهاج العمل في صناعة الجدل لأبي عبد الله اللآردي، و«كتاب المناظرات في الأسئلة والاعتراضات على أنواع الاستدلالات» لابن المعمار
Second: Research Horizons: This research is in reality only a beginning or a key to other researches whose features have appeared after completing the study of this topic. We can point here to some topics that can become fields for scientific research by researchers in the future: 1 - A group of studies have emerged that dealt with research on the topic of 'Dialectic in the Holy Quran' and covered the topic from almost all its aspects, but on the other hand we have not come across a book, thesis, or research related to dialectic in the noble Prophetic Sunnah. This is a very important topic of great significance, and it requires that a researcher or a group of researchers undertake to study it from its various aspects. 2 - The scholars of usul have authored a group of books specifically on dialectic, and we have discussed them very briefly in the introductory chapter. These books themselves need specific scientific studies for each one. Thus a group of researchers can each take one of the following topics, for example: 'Dialectic according to Imam al-Haramayn' or 'Dialectic according to al-Shirazi' or 'Dialectic according to al-Baji' or 'Dialectic according to Ibn Aqil' or 'Dialectic according to al-Tufi'. 3 - It is known that the Greeks had a method in dialectic, and this method was transmitted to the Islamic world when the Muslims translated the books of the Greeks starting from the era of the Caliph al-Ma'mun. So, was there a relationship between usuli dialectic and Greek dialectic? Were Muslim usul scholars influenced in their dialectical writings by the dialectical writings of the Greeks, especially Aristotle's works? Or do Muslim usul scholars have their own independent method that has no relation to the Greek method? This question is worthy of being raised, and it requires that a researcher or a group of researchers study this topic. It can be addressed under the title 'The Relationship of Usuli Dialectic to Aristotelian or Greek Dialectic', such that the research is comparative between the two methods. 4 - There are many books by usul scholars on dialectic that are still manuscripts and far from being reached by the hands of interested researchers. This requires that a group of students of knowledge and researchers in higher Islamic studies devote themselves to searching for these manuscripts in their locations and attempting to obtain them in their multiple copies - if they exist - then studying them scientifically, so that they are registered as university theses for Master's or Doctorate in the form of critical edition and study. We can point here, for example, to the book 'al-Muntahal fi al-Jadal' by Abu Hamid al-Ghazali, 'al-Munqidh min al-Dalal fi Masa'il al-Jadal' by Abd al-Aziz al-Nasafi, 'al-Jadal wa al-Kashif 'an Usul al-Dala'il wa Fusul al-'Ilal' by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, 'Minhaj al-Amal fi Sina'at al-Jadal' by Abu Abd Allah al-Lardi, and 'Kitab al-Munazarat fi al-As'ila wa al-I'tiradat 'ala Anwa' al-Istidlalat' by Ibn al-Mi'mar.
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage concludes the book or chapter by offering suggestions for future research in usuli dialectic. It is a forward-looking section, not a logical argument but a call to action. The author identifies four main areas: First, while dialectic in the Quran has been well-studied, dialectic in the Sunnah remains neglected and deserves comprehensive research. Second, the many specialized books on jadal by usul scholars (e.g., by Imam al-Haramayn, al-Shirazi, al-Baji, Ibn Aqil, al-Tufi) each require individual monographic studies. Third, the historical question of Greek influence on Islamic dialectic is posed: did Muslim usul scholars borrow from Aristotle and other Greeks, or did they develop an independent method? A comparative study is suggested. Fourth, many important manuscripts on jadal are still unpublished and need critical editions for graduate theses; specific examples are given, including works by al-Ghazali, al-Nasafi, al-Razi, al-Lardi, and Ibn al-Mi'mar. Each point is a direct recommendation, and the author provides concrete examples to guide future researchers.

الجدل الأرسطي
العلاقة بين الجدل الأصولي واليوناني

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

Critical Editions of Jadal Manuscripts
Author outlines four research topics: jadal in Sunnah, monographs, Greek influence, and manuscript studies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key unpublished jadal manuscripts and outline the steps for producing a critical edition.

Core Idea
Many foundational jadal texts are locked in manuscripts – editing them opens direct access to the tradition.

The author lists several important jadal works that remain in manuscript form. This lesson teaches you how to approach the task of critical edition (tahqiq) as a research contribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the manuscripts mentioned
The author names al-Muntahal by al-Ghazali, al-Munqidh by al-Nasafi, al-Jadal wa al-Kashif by al-Razi, Minhaj al-Amal by al-Lardi, and Kitab al-Munazarat by Ibn al-Mi'mar. Write down their titles and authors.
2
Understand the critical edition process
Learn the basic steps: locating manuscript copies, collating variants, establishing the text, adding commentary and introduction.
The author recommends producing editions as MA or PhD theses.
3
Assess the value of each manuscript
Explain why each manuscript is important: e.g., al-Ghazali's al-Muntahal is a major work by a seminal thinker.
Consider the author's stature and the work's content.
4
Create a project plan
Outline a timeline: find copies (6-12 months), collate (6 months), write introduction (3 months), etc.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
The Question of Greek Influence on Usuli Jadal
Author poses a comparative question about Greek and Islamic dialectic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to formulate a comparative research question about the relationship between usuli jadal and Greek dialectic.

Core Idea
The link between Greek and Islamic dialectic is an open question for researchers.

This passage raises a crucial comparative question: did Islamic legal theorists borrow from Greek dialectic, or did they develop an independent method? You are now equipped to frame this question for further investigation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two poles
Identify the two traditions being compared: Greek dialectic (especially Aristotelian) and usuli jadal as practiced by scholars like al-Juwayni and al-Shirazi.
Greek dialectic was transmitted through translations beginning in the Abbasid era.
2
Note the historical transmission
Recognize that Greek works were translated into Arabic, creating the possibility of influence. The author mentions the translation movement under al-Ma'mun.
This is a well-known historical fact.
3
Recognize the methodological contrast
The author presents two possibilities: either usuli jadal was influenced by Greek dialectic, or it is an independent development. Understand the stakes of each claim.
Independence would highlight originality; influence would show continuity.
4
Formulate a specific comparative hypothesis
Draft a testable research question, e.g., 'To what extent did Aristotle's Topics influence the structure of usuli jadal in the 5th/11th century?'
A good hypothesis guides the research.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من الباحثين لدراسته من جوانبه المختلفة. 2 - كتب علماء الأصول مجموعة من الكتب الخاصة بالجدل، وقد عرضنا للحديث عنها بصورة مختصرة جدا في الباب التمهيدي، وهذه الكتب تحتاج هي ذاتها إلى دراسات علمية خاصة بكل منها فيمكن لمجموعة من الباحثين أن يتناول كل منهم موضوعًا من الموضوعات الآتية مثلا : «الجدل عند إمام الحرمين» أو «الجدل عند الشيرازي» أو «الجدل عند الباجي» أو «الجدل عند ابن عقيل» أو الجدل عند الطوفي». 3 - معلوم أن اليونان كان عندهم منهج في الجدل وهذا المنهج انتقل إلى العالم الإسلامي عندما ترجم المسلمون كتب اليونان بداية من عصر المأمون الخليفة العباسي، فهل كانت للجدل الأصولي علاقة بالجدل اليوناني وهل تأثر الأصوليون المسلمون في كتاباتهم الجدلية بكتابات اليونانيين الجدلية، وخاصة منها مؤلفات أرسطو ؟ أم أن الأصوليين المسلمين لهم منهجهم المستقل الذي لا علاقة له بمنهج اليونان؟ إن هذا التساؤل جدير بالطرح، ويتطلب أن يقوم باحث أو مجموعة من الباحثين بدراسة هذا الموضوع ويمكن أن يتم تناوله تحت عنوان علاقة الجدل الأصولي بالجدل الأرسطي أو اليوناني»، بحيث يكون البحث مقارنا بين المنهجين . 4 هناك العديد من كتب الأصوليين في الجدل لا تزال مخطوطة وبعيدة عن أن تتناولها أيدي الباحثين المهتمين، وهذا يتطلب أن يتجرد مجموعة من طلاب العلم والباحثين في الدراسات العليا الشرعية للبحث عن هذه المخطوطات في مظانها ومحاولة الحصول عليها بنسخها المتعددة - إن وجدت - ثم دراستها دراسة علمية، بحيث يتم تسجيلها كرسائل جامعية للحصول على الماجستير أو الدكتوراه في شكل تحقيق ودراسة، ويمكن أن نشير هنا مثلا إلى كتاب «المنتحل في الجدل» لأبي حامد الغزالي، المنقذ من الذلل في مسائل الجدل» لعبد العزيز النسفي والجدل والكاشف عن أصول الدلائل وفصول العلل»، لفخر الدين الرازي، ومنهاج العمل في صناعة الجدل لأبي عبد الله اللآردي، و«كتاب المناظرات في الأسئلة والاعتراضات على أنواع الاستدلالات» لابن المعمار البغدادي، والقوانين الجلية في الاصطلاحات الجدلية، لابن الجزري، وغيرها من الكتب التي لم تطبع بعد من مؤلفات الأصوليين في الجدل. 5 الأحقاد يعيش عالمنا المعاصر صراعًا حادًا بين مختلف الاتجاهات الدينية أو الفكرية أو السياسية، وهذا الصراع كثيرًا ما يخرج عن طابعه المهذب ليتحول إلى حروب مستعرة، وهو ما يجعله لا ينتهي في العادة إلا إلى مزيد من والعداوات ; لذلك كان الإنسان المعاصر - أفرادا وجماعات - بحاجة إلى منهج الحوار وتبادل الرأي حول المسائل التي هي موضع خلاف حتى يمكن الوصول إلى تقارب وجهات النظر في شأنها وفي هذا الإطار يمكن الاستفادة من دراسة منهج الجدل عند الأصوليين، وخاصة الآداب التي حددوها للجدل، في وضع منهج معاصر للحوار يكون كفيلا بتحقيق النقاشات والحوارات لنتائجها المرجوة، وهنا يمكن لباحث ما أن يتناول موضوعًا بعنوان منهج الجدل الأصولي وعلاقته بالحوار المعاصر أو بأي عنوان آخر يختاره. تلك بعض الآفاق العلمية التي تحيل إليها هذه الرسالة، يمكن للباحثين في علم أصول الفقه ارتيادها وتناولها بالبحث والدراسة . وفي الختام أسال الله عز وجل أن يتقبل مني هذا العمل وأن ينفع به المسلمين عامة وطلبة العلوم الشرعية خاصة، وله سبحانه عز وجل الحمد والثناء في البدء والختام ، ومنه وحده رجاء الثواب الجزيل يوم القيامة إنه عز وجل خير مسؤول وأعظم مأمول . وصل اللهم وسلم وبارك على عبدك ونبيك محمد وعلى الله وصحبه أجمعين، وآخر دعوانا أن الحمد لله رب العالمين.
From the researchers to study it from its various aspects. 2 - The scholars of usul authored a set of books on jadal, and we have presented a very brief discussion of them in the introductory chapter. It can be addressed under the title 'The relationship of usuli jadal with Aristotelian or Greek dialectic', such that the research is comparative between the two methods. 4 - There are many books by usulis on jadal that remain in manuscript form and far from the hands of interested researchers. This requires a group of students and researchers in higher Islamic studies to search for these manuscripts in their repositories and attempt to obtain them in their multiple copies - if available - then study them scientifically, so that they become university theses for master's or doctorate in the form of editing and study. We can point here, for example, to the book 'al-Muntahal fi al-Jadal' by Abu Hamid al-Ghazali, 'al-Munqidh min al-Dalal fi Masa'il al-Jadal' by 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Nasafi, 'al-Jadal wa al-Kashif 'an Usul al-Dala'il wa Fusul al-'Ilal' by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, 'Minhaj al-'Amal fi Sina'at al-Jadal' by Abu 'Abd Allah al-Lardi, 'Kitab al-Munazarat fi al-As'ilah wa al-I'tiradat 'ala Anwa' al-Istidlalat' by Ibn al-Mi'mar al-Baghdadi, 'al-Qawanin al-Jaliyyah fi al-Istilahat al-Jadaliyyah' by Ibn al-Jazari, and other books by usulis on jadal that have not yet been printed. 5 - Resentments? Our contemporary world lives a sharp conflict between various religious, intellectual, or political trends. This conflict often deviates from its civil character and turns into raging wars, which usually ends only in more enmities. Therefore, contemporary man - individuals and groups - needs a method of dialogue and exchange of opinions on matters of disagreement so that convergence of viewpoints can be reached. In this framework, studying the method of jadal among the usulis, especially the etiquettes they defined for jadal, can be utilized in developing a contemporary method for dialogue that can bring discussions and dialogues to their desired results. Here a researcher can take a topic titled 'The usuli jadal method and its relationship with contemporary dialogue' or any other title he chooses. These are some of the scientific horizons that this thesis points to; they can be explored and studied by researchers in usul al-fiqh. In conclusion, I ask Allah Almighty to accept this work from me and to benefit Muslims in general and students of shar'i sciences in particular. To Him, glory be, is praise and gratitude in the beginning and the end. From Him alone is hope for great reward on the Day of Judgment. He is the best to ask and the greatest to hope for. O Allah, send blessings and peace upon Your servant and Prophet Muhammad, and upon his family and all his Companions. And our final call is that all praise is due to Allah, Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage is the concluding section of the book, where the author presents several proposed research directions for future scholars interested in the study of jadal (dialectic) among the usuliyyin (Islamic legal theorists). The author first mentions that the books by usuli scholars on jadal warrant individual specialized studies, giving examples of potential monographs on specific figures like al-Juwayni (Imam al-Haramayn), al-Shirazi, al-Baji, Ibn 'Aqil, and al-Tufi. This suggests a historical approach. Second, the author raises a comparative question: is usuli jadal indebted to Greek dialectic, particularly Aristotle, or is it an independent Islamic development? This invites comparative analysis. Third, the author points to many unpublished manuscripts on jadal, listing several titles (e.g., al-Ghazali's al-Muntahal, al-Razi's al-Jadal wa al-Kashif) and encourages researchers to edit and study them for higher degrees. Fourth, the author suggests that the etiquettes of jadal developed by usulis can inform a contemporary method of dialogue to mitigate conflicts in the modern world, citing the need for civil disagreement. The passage concludes with a traditional prayer and praise to Allah. The overall thrust is a call to action for researchers in usul al-fiqh to further explore the rich tradition of dialectic in Islamic legal theory.

The Manuscript Treasure and Contemporary Dialogue Potential
Author lists manuscripts and suggests modern application.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify unpublished manuscripts on jadal and propose how the etiquette of jadal can inform modern dialogue.

Core Idea
Unpublished jadal manuscripts hold keys to both historical understanding and modern conflict resolution.

The author points to many unedited manuscripts and suggests that the adab of jadal can address contemporary polarisation. This lesson explores these two concrete research agendas.

Guided Path
1
List the mentioned manuscript titles
Identify the manuscripts named: al-Muntahal, al-Munqidh min al-Dalal, al-Jadal wa al-Kashif, Minhaj al-'Amal, Kitab al-Munazarat, al-Qawanin al-Jaliyyah.
These are all works on jadal by usuli scholars.
2
Recognize the need for critical editions
Understand that these manuscripts are unpublished and require scholarly editing (tahqiq) to become accessible.
Editing involves collating copies, verifying text, and adding critical apparatus.
3
Identify the etiquettes of jadal
Recall the rules of adab al-jadal taught in this tradition (e.g., fairness, respecting opponent, sequential arguments). The author suggests these can guide modern civil dialogue.
The etiquettes are a practical outcome of the theoretical study.
4
Envision a contemporary application
Propose how usuli jadal etiquettes might be adapted for modern interfaith or political discussions to reduce conflict.
The author frames this as a research topic.

From the researchers to study it from its various aspects. 2 - The scholars of usul authored a set of books on jadal, and we have presented a very brief discussion of them in the introductory chapter. Relevance of Usuli Jadal for Contemporary Dialogue
Author concludes with reflections on conflict and call for dialogue.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the etiquettes of jadal as developed by usuliyyun can be adapted to construct a contemporary framework for productive dialogue on religious and intellectual disagreements.

Core Idea
Jadal's adab offers a proven, rigorous framework for resolving modern conflicts through principled dialogue.

In the conclusion of his work, the author steps back from technical details and addresses the contemporary crisis of sharp conflicts in religious, intellectual, and political spheres. He argues that the discipline of jadal, particularly its ethical guidelines (adab), provides a model for constructive dialogue. This lesson explores how the classical jadal tradition can be applied to modern needs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem: contemporary conflict
The author describes sharp conflicts leading to hatreds. What is the nature of these conflicts? Recognize that the author sees current conflicts as destructive and lacking civil discourse.
The author mentions 'religious, intellectual, or political trends'.
2
Recognize the solution proposed: jadal methodology
The author suggests studying the methodology of jadal among usuliyyun, especially their etiquettes (adab). Identify why jadal—a classical science of debate—is presented as a remedy.
Adab include fairness, respect for opponent, seeking truth, and structured argument.
3
Analyze the transfer: from classical usul to modern dialogue
Explain how the adab of jadal can be adapted to contemporary dialogue. Consider specific principles such as al-insaf (fairness), al-taraddud (responsiveness), and the goal of reaching truth.
The author suggests a research topic: 'Methodology of Usuli Dialectic and its Relation to Contemporary Dialogue'.
4
Evaluate the potential: research horizons
The author invites researchers to explore this connection. Assess the feasibility and challenges of applying a medieval Islamic debate framework to modern global issues.
Think about differences in context, but the core ethical guidelines remain relevant.

الجدل

البغدادي، والقوانين الجلية في الاصطلاحات الجدلية، لابن الجزري، وغيرها من الكتب التي لم تطبع بعد من مؤلفات الأصوليين في الجدل.

يعيش عالمنا المعاصر صراعًا حادًا بين مختلف الاتجاهات الدينية أو الفكرية أو السياسية، وهذا الصراع كثيرًا ما يخرج عن طابعه المهذب ليتحول إلى حروب مستعرة، وهو ما يجعله لا ينتهي في العادة إلا إلى مزيد من العداوات؛ لذلك كان الإنسان المعاصر - أفرادا وجماعات - بحاجة إلى منهج الحوار وتبادل الرأي حول المسائل التي هي موضع خلاف حتى يمكن الوصول إلى تقارب وجهات النظر في شأنها وفي هذا الإطار يمكن الاستفادة من دراسة منهج الجدل عند الأصوليين، وخاصة الآداب التي حددوها للجدل، في وضع منهج معاصر للحوار يكون كفيلا بتحقيق النقاشات والحوارات لنتائجها المرجوة، وهنا يمكن لباحث ما أن يتناول موضوعًا بعنوان منهج الجدل الأصولي وعلاقته بالحوار المعاصر أو بأي عنوان آخر يختاره. تلك بعض الآفاق العلمية التي تحيل إليها هذه الرسالة، يمكن للباحثين في علم أصول الفقه ارتيادها وتناولها بالبحث والدراسة . وفي الختام أسأل الله عز وجل أن يتقبل مني هذا العمل وأن ينفع به المسلمين عامة وطلبة العلوم الشرعية خاصة، وله سبحانه عز وجل الحمد والثناء في البدء والختام ، ومنه وحده رجاء الثواب الجزيل يوم القيامة إنه عز وجل خير مسؤول وأعظم مأمول . وصل اللهم وسلم وبارك على عبدك ونبيك محمد وعلى آله وصحبه أجمعين، وآخر دعوانا أن الحمد لله رب العالمين.

ثم الفهارس العامة:
أولا: فهرس الآيات القرآنية
ثانيا: فهرس الأحاديث النبوية
ثالثا: فهرس الآثار
رابعا: فهرس الأشعار
خامسا: فهرس المصطلحات
سادسا: فهرس القواعد والمسائل الأصولية
سابعا: فهرس الأحكام والمسائل الفقهية
ثامنا: فهرس الأعلام
تاسعا: فهرس الكتب المذكورة في المتن
عاشرا: قائمة المصادر والمراجع
حادي عشر: فهرس الموضوعات
The contemporary world lives a sharp conflict between various religious, intellectual, or political trends, and this conflict often departs from its civil character to turn into raging wars, which usually only results in more hatreds. Therefore contemporary man - individuals and groups - is in need of a methodology of dialogue and exchange of opinions on issues that are subject to disagreement, so that convergence of views can be reached. In this framework, benefit can be derived from studying the methodology of jadal among the usuliyyun, especially the etiquettes they defined for jadal, in developing a contemporary methodology of dialogue that can ensure discussions and dialogues achieve their desired outcomes. Here a researcher can take up a topic entitled 'The Methodology of Usuli Dialectic and its Relation to Contemporary Dialogue' or any other title he chooses. These are some of the scholarly horizons to which this treatise points; researchers in usul al-fiqh can explore them and take them up for research and study. In conclusion, I ask Allah Almighty to accept this work from me and to benefit Muslims in general and students of Islamic sciences in particular, and to Him be praise and gratitude in the beginning and the end, and from Him alone is the hope of great reward on the Day of Resurrection. He is the best to ask and the greatest to hope for. O Allah, send blessings upon Your servant and Prophet Muhammad and upon his family and all his companions. Our last call is that all praise is due to Allah, Lord of the worlds.

Commentary
This passage is the concluding section of the book. It begins with a footnote-like reference to other works on jadal by al-Baghdadi, Ibn al-Jazari, and others that remain unpublished. Then the author moves to a main paragraph titled 'Al-Ahqad' (Hatreds), though the title may be a miscopy of 'Al-Khatima' (Conclusion). In this paragraph, the author reflects on the intense conflicts in the contemporary world and argues that a methodology of dialogue based on the principles of jadal (dialectical debate) as developed by the usuliyyun (Islamic legal theorists) can provide a constructive approach to resolving disputes. The author emphasizes the ethical guidelines (adab) that scholars of jadal established, which can be adapted to modern dialogue to achieve productive outcomes. He suggests a potential research topic: 'The Methodology of Usuli Dialectic and its Relation to Contemporary Dialogue.' The author then thanks Allah and expresses hope for the work's acceptance and benefit. Finally, the passage lists the general indexes included in the book, covering Quranic verses, hadiths, reports, poems, terms, usul al-fiqh rules, fiqh rulings, prominent figures, books mentioned, sources, and topics. This section is not a logical teaching but a closing statement that highlights the practical relevance of jadal studies.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Eleven indices unlock the entire content of a classical Islamic scholarly work.

This front-matter page from 'Jadal Usuliyyin' presents a systematic list of indices that guide the reader through the book's vast content. Memorizing these indices helps you quickly locate Quranic verses, hadith, technical terms, and more. In this lesson, you will work through the list analytically so that you can recall each index and understand its function in Islamic scholarship.

1
Count the indices from the Arabic text
Read the Arabic list from 'أولا' to 'حادي عشر'. Count how many items are listed. Note that the author starts with Quranic verses and ends with subject index.
The list uses ordinal numbers (أولا، ثانيا، etc.).
2
Categorize indices by type of content
Group the indices: scriptural sources (Quran, hadith, reports), literary (poems), technical (terms, usul rules, fiqh rulings), and references (figures, books, sources, subjects).
This helps in understanding the scope of the book's references.
3
Identify the purpose of each index
For each index, ask: what would a reader use this for? For example, 'Index of Quranic Verses' helps locate verses cited in the text; 'Index of Terms' helps find definitions.
This deepens appreciation of the work's organization.
4
Test your recall without looking
Cover the Arabic and try to recite the eleven indices in order. Then check against the text. Repeat until fluent.
Memorization anchor – this is key for quick navigation.

Jadal. General Indices. First: Index of Quranic Verses. Second: Index of Prophetic Hadiths. Third: Index of Reports (Athar). Fourth: Index of Poems. Fifth: Index of Terms. Sixth: Index of Usul Rules and Issues. Seventh: Index of Fiqh Rulings and Issues. Eighth: Index of Notable Figures. Ninth: Index of Books Mentioned in the Text. Tenth: List of Sources and References. Eleventh: Index of Subjects.

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter listing of the indices found at the end of the book 'Jadal Usuliyyin'. The author enumerates eleven indices covering Quranic verses, hadith, reports, poems, technical terms, usul al-fiqh rules, fiqh rulings, notable figures (a'lam), books cited, sources/references, and subjects. Such indices are standard in classical Islamic scholarly works to facilitate navigation of the text. This page serves as a practical guide for readers seeking specific content within the book.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
How to Use the Quranic Verse Index in Jadal Works
Front matter index of Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to locate any Quranic verse referenced in the book Jadal Usuliyyin using the provided index, and identify the surah and partial verse text.

Core Idea
An index is a navigational tool – knowing how to read it saves time and ensures accurate reference.

This lesson introduces the index of Quranic verses found at the beginning of the book Jadal Usuliyyin. While not a logical argument in itself, this index is an essential tool for any student of dialectical argumentation (jadal), as it allows quick access to the Quranic evidence that underpins the debates in the main text. Understanding its structure will help you efficiently cross-reference verses during your studies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the title and purpose
The index is titled 'فهرس الآيات القرآنية' (Index of Quranic Verses) under the heading 'الجدل' (Dialectic). It lists verses cited in the book.
2
Locate the surah and verse snippet
Each surah is introduced by its name and number (e.g., سورة البقرة (2)). Following are partial verse texts with ellipses. Find the surah you need, then scan the verses listed.
3
Note the verse for cross-reference
The index provides enough of the verse to identify it. Use the surah and partial text to locate the full verse in the Quran. This allows you to see the exact wording used in the author's arguments.

Dialectic: First: Index of Quranic Verses. - Surah al-Baqarah (2) - 'It is He who created for you all that is on the earth...' - 'And when your Lord said to the angels, Indeed I am going to place...' And say: 'Whoever is an enemy to Gabriel...' 'Whatever verse We abrogate or cause to be forgotten...' 'So pardon and forgive...' - 'And whoever is granted remission from his brother...' 'Say, I do not find in what has been revealed to me anything forbidden...'

Commentary
This passage is a front matter index of Quranic verses cited in the book Jadal Usuliyyin. It begins with the heading 'First: Index of Quranic Verses' under the title 'al-Jadal'. The index lists verses from Surah al-Baqarah (2) through Surah al-An'am (6), including partial quotations and ellipses. Each surah is introduced by its name and number, followed by selected verses that are likely referenced in the main text of the book. The verses cover a range of legal, theological, and narrative topics, such as creation, prayer, fasting, marriage, divorce, usury, pilgrimage, dietary laws, and disputes with non-believers. The index serves as a quick reference for readers to locate the Quranic evidence used in the dialectical arguments (jadal) presented in the book.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
10 min
Quranic Evidence in Jadal
Author lists Quranic verses used as evidence in jadal arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of Quranic verses as textual evidence in jadal and organize them by legal topic.

Core Idea
Quranic verses are the supreme authority in jadal; knowing them is essential for sound argumentation.

In jadal (dialectical argumentation), every claim must be supported by authoritative texts. The Quran is the primary source. This lesson introduces a list of verses compiled for use in debates. You will learn how to recognize these verses and understand their relevance to specific legal and theological issues.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the purpose of the list
This passage is a compilation of Quranic verses that the author intends as raw material for jadal arguments. In a debate, you must cite authoritative texts; the Quran is the highest authority. Memorizing these verses prepares you to support your positions.
The list is not exhaustive but covers key topics.
2
Scan and identify thematic categories
As you read through the verses, note the legal or theological topics addressed: marriage (e.g., فَانكِحُوا مَا طَابَ لَكُمْ), inheritance (e.g., وَإِنْ كَانَ رَجُلٌ يُورَثُ كَلَالَةً), purity (e.g., فَتَيَمَّمُوا صَعِيدًا طَيِّبًا), criminal law (e.g., وَمَنْ قَتَلَ مُؤْمِنًا خَطَأً), and prohibition of intoxicants (e.g., إِنَّمَا الْخَمْرُ وَالْمَيْسِرُ). Grouping them will help you retrieve the correct verse quickly in a debate.
Some verses cover multiple topics.
3
Connect each verse to a potential jadal claim
For each verse, ask: What claim could this verse support? For instance, the verse about marrying up to four wives (مَثْنَىٰ وَثُلَاثَ وَرُبَاعَ) can be used to argue for the permissibility of polygamy under certain conditions. Practicing this mental link trains you to use evidence effectively.
In jadal, the opponent may challenge the interpretation, so prepare responses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالَّذِينَ قَالُوا إِنَّ اللَّهَ عَهِدَ إِلَيْنَا أَلَّا نُؤْمِنَ لِرَسُولٍ ... فَانكِحُوا مَا طَابَ لَكُمْ مِنَ النِّسَاءِ مَثْنَىٰ وَثُلَاثَ وَرُبَاعَ ... وَإِنْ كَانَ رَجُلٌ يُورَثُ كَلَالَةً أَوِ امْرَأَةٌ ... وَأَنْ تَجْمَعُوا بَيْنَ الْأُخْتَيْنِ ... وَمَنْ لَمْ يَسْتَطِعْ مِنْكُمْ طَوْلًا ... وَإِنْ كُنْتُمْ مَرْضَىٰ أَوْ عَلَىٰ سَفَرٍ ... وَمَنْ قَتَلَ مُؤْمِنًا خَطَأً فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مُؤْمِنَةٍ ... وَمَنْ يُشَاقِقِ الرَّسُولَ مِنْ بَعْدِ مَا تَبَيَّنَ لَهُ الْهُدَىٰ ... يَسْأَلُكَ أَهْلُ الْكِتَابِ أَنْ تُنَزِّلَ عَلَيْهِمْ ... وَإِذَا حَلَلْتُمْ فَاصْطَادُوا ... وَحُرِّمَتْ عَلَيْكُمُ الْمَيْتَةُ ... وَمَا أَكَلَ السَّبُعُ إِلَّا مَا ذَكَّيْتُمْ ... وَالْمُحْصَنَاتُ مِنَ الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْكِتَابَ ... وَامْسَحُوا بِرُءُوسِكُمْ ... فَتَيَمَّمُوا صَعِيدًا طَيِّبًا ... وَكَتَبْنَا عَلَيْهِمْ فِيهَا أَنَّ النَّفْسَ بِالنَّفْسِ ... لَقَدْ كَفَرَ الَّذِينَ قَالُوا إِنَّ اللَّهَ ثَالِثُ ثَلَاثَةٍ ... يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِنَّمَا الْخَمْرُ وَالْمَيْسِرُ ... يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لَا تَقْتُلُوا الصَّيْدَ وَأَنْتُمْ حُرُمٌ ... يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا شَهَادَةُ بَيْنِكُمْ إِذَا حَضَرَ ... وَمِنْهُمْ مَنْ يَسْتَمِعُ إِلَيْكَ وَجَعَلْنَا عَلَىٰ قُلُوبِهِمْ ... وَلَقَدْ جِئْتُمُونَا فُرَادَىٰ كَمَا خَلَقْنَاكُمْ أَوَّلَ مَرَّةٍ ... وَآتُوا حَقَّهُ يَوْمَ حَصَادِهِ ... ثَمَانِيَةَ أَزْوَاجٍ مِنَ الضَّأْنِ اثْنَيْنِ ... قُلْ لَا أَجِدُ فِي مَا أُوحِيَ إِلَيَّ مُحَرَّمًا ... وَلَقَدْ خَلَقْنَاكُمْ ثُمَّ صَوَّرْنَاكُمْ ... وَكُلُوا وَاشْرَبُوا ... وَاتَّبِعُوهُ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَهْتَدُونَ ... أَوَلَمْ يَنْظُرُوا فِي مَلَكُوتِ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ ... وَخُذِ الْعَفْوَ ... وَإِذَا قُرِئَ الْقُرْآنُ فَاسْتَمِعُوا لَهُ ... وَمَا كَانَ لِنَبِيٍّ أَنْ يَكُونَ لَهُ أَسْرَىٰ ... فَاقْتُلُوا الْمُشْرِكِينَ ... قُلِ انْظُرُوا مَاذَا فِي السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ ... قُرْآنًا عَرَبِيًّا ... وَاتَّبَعْتُ مِلَّةَ آبَائِي إِبْرَاهِيمَ وَإِسْحَاقَ وَيَعْقُوبَ ... قُلْ هَٰذِهِ سَبِيلِي ... وَكَذَٰلِكَ أَنْزَلْنَاهُ حُكْمًا عَرَبِيًّا ... وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَا مِنْ رَسُولٍ إِلَّا بِلِسَانِ قَوْمِهِ ... قَالَتْ رُسُلُهُمْ أَفِي اللَّهِ شَكٌّ ... أَلَمْ يَأْتِكُمْ نَبَأُ الَّذِينَ مِنْ قَبْلِكُمْ قَوْمِ نُوحٍ وَعَادٍ وَثَمُودَ Commentary
This passage presents a compilation of Quranic verses that the author intends to use as primary evidence in dialectical arguments (jadal). The verses cover a wide range of legal and theological topics, including marriage, inheritance, purity, retaliation, polytheism, and more. In jadal, the debater must ground arguments in authoritative texts, and the Quran is the supreme authority. By listing these verses, the author provides the raw material for constructing arguments. The student of jadal should memorize these and similar verses to be able to cite them in debate. The listing is not argumentative in itself but serves as a resource.

Using the Quranic Verse Index in Jadal Studies
Listing of Quranic verses with page references for use in jadal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to locate and apply a Quranic verse from the index as evidence in a jadal argument on a given topic.

Core Idea
A verse index is your roadmap to Quranic evidence in dialectical reasoning.

This passage is an index of Quranic verses cited in a work on jadal (dialectical theology). While it appears as a simple list, it is a powerful tool for quickly finding the scriptural backing used in debates. In this lesson, you will learn how to navigate such an index to support your own arguments in Islamic dialectics.

Guided Path
1
Identify the surah and verse number
The index lists surah names and numbers. First, note the surah and the verse fragment provided. For example, 'سورة النحل (16) - ﴿فَلا تَضْرِبُوا لِلَّهِ الْأَمْثَالَ﴾' gives you Surah An-Nahl, verse 16:74.
The verse fragment is the beginning of the cited passage; use it to locate the full verse in the Quran.
2
Understand the verse's role in the original debate
The index is from a book on jadal. Look up the page number (not fully preserved here) to read the author's argument that uses this verse. Note how the verse supports or refutes a position.
The verse is not neutral; it is deployed within a specific logical context.
3
Apply the verse to a new jadal scenario
Practice by taking a common jadal topic—e.g., the permissibility of analogical reasoning (qiyas) for Allah. The verse 16:74 'So do not attribute to Allah examples' is often used to limit analogy. Use it to construct a brief objection or response.
Always check the verse's tafsir to ensure correct application.
4
Cross-reference with other verses in the index
The index includes multiple verses on related themes. For the topic of divine attributes, also check Surah Al-Ikhlas or Surah Ash-Shura. Combining evidence strengthens your argument.
The index is not exhaustive; use your knowledge of the Quran to supplement.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Role of Scriptural Evidence in Jadal
List of Quranic verses and prophetic hadiths cited in the book

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Quranic verses and hadiths are essential as evidence in jadal (dialectical disputation) within usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Jadal is grounded in revelation, not mere logic.

This lesson introduces you to the appendix of 'Jadal Usuliyyin', which lists Quranic verses and hadiths cited in the book. While this may seem like a dry index, it reveals a key principle: in Islamic dialectical argumentation, every claim must be anchored in scriptural sources. Understanding this list helps you appreciate how jadal operates within the bounds of revelation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sections of the index
Note that the index is divided into Quranic verses (by surah) and prophetic hadiths. This tells you that the author draws evidence from both primary sources of Islamic law.
The Quranic verses are listed by surah number, and hadiths are listed without specific chains.
2
Observe the variety of topics covered
The verses touch on hypocrisy, divorce, resurrection, and creation. The hadiths cover purity, prayer, fasting, inheritance, and more. This range shows that jadal is not limited to one area of fiqh; it applies broadly.
Each citation likely corresponds to an argument made earlier in the book.
3
Recognize the function of the index
The index serves as a reference tool. When studying jadal, you can trace back arguments to their scriptural foundations. This reinforces that jadal is not abstract reasoning but evidence-based debate.
In usul al-fiqh, the strength of a jadal argument depends on the authenticity and relevance of its scriptural support.
4
Understand the link to usul al-fiqh
Jadal in usul al-fiqh is a method for defending or challenging legal rulings using proofs. These proofs are primarily from the Quran and Sunnah. This index exemplifies that principle.
Without scriptural grounding, a jadal argument would be considered weak or invalid.

This passage is an appendix or index listing the Quranic verses and prophetic hadiths that are cited within the book 'Jadal Usuliyyin'. The section begins with the title 'الجدل' (Dialectic) and then lists surahs with their numbers and partial verses, followed by a second section titled 'فهرس الأحاديث النبوية' (Index of Prophetic Hadiths) containing numerous hadiths on various legal topics. The hadiths cover rulings on purity, prayer, fasting, inheritance, and other fiqh matters. As a teaching tool, this list reminds the student that jadal (dialectical reasoning) in the Islamic tradition is always grounded in scriptural evidence from the Quran and Sunnah. The author's choice of these particular sources likely reflects the arguments made earlier in the book.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Using the Index of Legal Opinions (Fihris al-Athar) in Jadal
Author presents an alphabetical index of legal opinions from Companions and early jurists.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to locate a legal opinion (athar) from an alphabetical index and explain how it functions as evidence in a jadal debate.

Core Idea
The fihris al-athar is a debater's toolbox: every opinion is a live weapon in argumentation.

In jadal, citing a Companion's or early jurist's opinion can strengthen or refute a position. But how do you find the right opinion quickly? This lesson introduces the fihris al-athar, an alphabetical index of such opinions. By learning to navigate it, you gain a practical skill for constructing and challenging arguments in usul al-fiqh debates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Letter Categories
The index is organized alphabetically by the first letter of the narrator's name or the topic. For example, entries under 'A' relate to issues starting with alif (such as 'ayyuma imra'atin...') or narrators like Ali.
2
Locate the Relevant Entry
For a given legal question, find which companion's opinion is listed. For instance, under 'A' there are multiple opinions on the iddah of a woman who remarries during her waiting period.
The index provides the opinion and the source in parentheses.
3
Extract the Legal Ruling
Each entry contains a concise ruling. For Ali's opinion, it says 'She observes the iddah of the longer of the two terms' (تعتد بأبعد الأجلين).
Note the difference between opinions from Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Umar.
4
Relate the Opinion to a Jadal Argument
Consider how this athar could be used as evidence. In a debate on the iddah, an arguer might cite Ali's opinion to support a specific ruling.
Opponents might counter with Ibn Mas'ud's opinion that she waits until delivery.
5
Assess the Strength of the Athar
In jadal, the authority of the companion and the clarity of the report matter. Ali's opinion carries weight, but later jurists might prefer Umar's view.
Understanding the hierarchy of companions helps in evaluating athar.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثالثا : فهرس الآثار
- أ -
أيما امرأة نكحت في عدتها فإن كان زوجها ...

تعتد بوضع الحمل (ابن مسعود)
تعتد من الأول بقية العدة ثم تستقبل العدة من الثاني (عمر وعلي)
- ج
جلدتها بكتاب الله، ورجمتها بسنة نبي الله (علي)
- ع
عجبا لابن عمرو هذا يأمر النساء إذا اغتسلن أن ينقضن رؤوسهن
- ق
قال عمر فيمن ظاهر من أربع نسوة أنه تلزمه كفارة واحدة
- ك
كان زوج بريرة حرا (عائشة)
كنت أفرك المني من ثوب رسول الله وهو يصلي عليه (عائشة)
- ل
لا ترد الحرة بعيب (عبد الله بن مسعود)
- و
ورث عثمان تماضر بنت الأصبغ الكلبية ورث عثمان تماضر، وأما أنا فلا أرى توريث المبتوتة (ابن الزبير)
Third: Index of Narrations (Athar)
- A -
Any woman who marries during her waiting period, if her husband...
She observes the iddah of the longer of the two terms (Ali)
She observes the iddah until delivery (Ibn Mas'ud)
She completes the iddah from the first husband then begins a new iddah from the second (Umar and Ali)
- J
I flogged her by the Book of Allah and stoned her by the Sunnah of Allah's Prophet (Ali)
- Ayn
I am amazed at Ibn Amr ordering women when they bathe to untie their hair
- Q
Umar said concerning a man who practiced dhihar from four women that one expiation is binding on him
- K
Barira's husband was free (Aisha)
I used to rub off the semen from the garment of Allah's Messenger while he was praying (Aisha)
- L
A free woman is not returned due to a defect (Abdullah ibn Mas'ud)
- W
Uthman inherited Tamadur bint al-Asbagh al-Kalbiyya... Uthman inherited Tamadur, but as for me, I do not consider inheritance for the irrevocably divorced woman (Ibn al-Zubayr)
Source pages p. 519

Commentary
This passage presents an index (fihris) of legal opinions (athar) arranged alphabetically by the first letter of the narrator or topic. Such indices are common in usul al-fiqh and jadal works to provide quick reference to authoritative precedents from the Companions and early jurists. Each entry typically includes a concise statement of the legal ruling and the source (Companion or scholar) in parentheses. For example, under the letter 'A' we find opinions on the waiting period (iddah) of a woman who marries during her iddah, attributed to Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Umar with Ali. Under 'J' is Ali's famous statement regarding the flogging and stoning of a adulteress. Under 'K' are two narrations from Aisha: one about Barira's husband being free, and another about rubbing off semen from the Prophet's garment. These athar serve as evidence (adilla) in dialectical arguments (jadal) among usuliyyin, where each party cites such precedents to support their position. The index allows debaters to locate relevant precedents quickly.

فهرس الآثار

Key Takeaway
The fihris al-athar is a practical tool for jadal, organizing authoritative legal opinions for quick citation and argumentation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Navigating the Fihris al-Ash'ar: Using Poetry Indices in Jadal Works
This is the index of poems cited in the book with page numbers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to locate a specific poetic verse cited in the book al-Jadal using its index of poems.

Core Idea
An index is a scholar's compass to find evidence in classical texts.

In Islamic dialectic (jadal), poets often cite verses as rhetorical or analogical evidence. The index of poems (fihris al-ash'ar) at the back of a work organizes these citations alphabetically, making them easy to find. This lesson teaches you how to use such an index efficiently, a skill essential for navigating reference works in the Islamic scholarly tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first letter of the poem's opening word or poet's name
In the index, entries are grouped alphabetically by the first letter of the verse's first word (or sometimes the poet's name). For example, a poem starting with 'إذا' would be under the letter 'Alif'.
The index in our source uses Arabic alphabet order: أ, ب, ت, etc.
2
Scan the entries under that letter to find your poem
Under each letter, entries list the first few words of the verse followed by the page number. Look for the phrase that matches your target verse.
OCR may misread numerals; verify page numbers carefully.
3
Note the page number(s) associated with the verse
The index provides one or more page numbers where the verse is cited. Record them to locate the verse in the main text.
In the given index, most entries have a single page number (e.g., 139, 137).
4
Turn to the specified page and read the verse in context
On the indicated page, the verse will be embedded in a jadal argument or example. Read the surrounding text to understand how the author uses the verse as evidence.
The index is a tool for quick reference; the main text provides the logical context.

The index demonstrates the integration of Arabic poetry as a source of rhetorical and logical examples in Islamic dialectic.

Navigating the Fihris al-Mustalahat
Fifth section: Index of terms from the book on jadal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to locate any technical term in this index and cross-reference its page numbers to find its discussion in the book.

Core Idea
The index is your roadmap: find the term, read the page, unlock the concept.

Every serious work of Islamic scholarship includes a fihris al-mustalahat – an index of technical terms. This passage is exactly that: a list of the key terms used in the book on jadal, each followed by page numbers. Knowing how to read this index is the first step to using the book effectively. Let's parse it together.

Guided Path
1
Scan the alphabetical or thematic order
Notice that the terms are not listed alphabetically but seem to follow the order of appearance in the book. Look for the first term 'الجدل' – it appears at the top, indicating the central topic.
Some indices are alphabetical; this one follows the book's sequence.
2
Identify the page numbers
After each term, you see numbers like '52..' or '467 .466 .286 .208 .92 .77 .76.75'. These are page references. The dots indicate missing or unclear digits (often due to printing).
In your copy, the numbers may be clearer; use them to jump to discussions.
3
Group related terms
Observe that some terms are conceptually linked: e.g., 'الانتقال المحمود' and 'الانتقال المذموم' (praiseworthy and blameworthy transition). Recognising these groups helps you see the structure of the book.
Jadal discussions often proceed by paired opposites.
4
Note the categories of breaking off (انقطاع)
Many terms begin with 'الانقطاع' followed by different causes. This tells you that the book dedicates a section to various ways an argument can break down – a key topic in jadal.
Each subtype is a clue to the author's analytical framework.

This is a valuable reference for students of jadal to locate definitions and discussions.

Navigating the Jadal Index: Key Terms and Scope
Lists key terms and topics covered in the book's index.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key terms in the index of Jadal Usuliyyin and explain the significance of the term 'al-inqitā‘' in dialectical debate.

Core Idea
An index reveals the conceptual architecture of a discipline.

This lesson introduces you to the index of the classical work 'Jadal Usuliyyin' (Dialectics of the Legal Theorists). While an index may seem like a mere list, it actually maps the whole field of jadal. We'll focus on one important term, al-inqitā‘ (disconnection), and its many subtypes, to see how the tradition classified debate outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Scan the index entries under the letter 'alif'
Look at the terms starting with 'إ' (إبطال الدور والتسلسل, الإجماع, etc.). Notice how they cover foundational concepts like circularity rebuttal and consensus.
The index is arranged by Arabic root letters.
2
Locate the term 'al-inqitā‘' and its subtypes
Find 'الانقطاع' and the list that follows: by clarification, denial, etc. Count the subtypes. This shows the detailed classification of debate 'disconnections'.
There are 8 subtypes listed, from 'بالاستفسار' to 'بالمسابة'.
3
Identify terms related to definition (ta‘rif)
Spot 'التعريف', 'التعريف بالتقسيم', 'التعريف بالتمييز', 'التعريف بالضد أو بالتضاد', 'التعريف بالمثال', and 'الحد'. Observe the variety of definition methods.
This indicates the importance of proper definition in jadal.
4
Analyze the scope of the index
Note that the index includes not only debate moves but also sources of law (الإجماع, الاستصحاب), reasoning tools (الاستدلال, الأقيسة الإضمارية), and fallacies (الحيل والمغالطات). This shows jadal integrates many aspects of usul al-fiqh.
The discipline is not just about argumentation but covers evidence and inference.

This passage is the index of terms from the book 'Jadal Usuliyyin' (Dialectics of the Legal Theorists). It provides a classified list of the key concepts and topics covered in the work, arranged alphabetically by Arabic root letters. The index begins with the letter 'alif' (إبطال الدور والتسلسل, etc.), then 'ba' (البناء), 'ta' (التأثير), 'jim' (الجدل), and so on. The terms reflect the core concerns of the discipline: methods of argumentation (الاستدلال, الاستقراء, الاستصحاب), types of transitions (الانتقال المحمود والمذموم), definitions (التعريف), and specific techniques in dialectical debate (الانقطاع, الإلزام). This index serves as a roadmap for students navigating the book, showing the breadth of jadal topics discussed. It is a front matter passage intended for reference, not direct instruction.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
An index is a map of the discipline's conceptual landscape.

This index may look like a dry list of terms and numbers, but it is actually a powerful tool. It reveals which topics the author considers central and how they are organized. Learning to read such an index helps you quickly locate and understand the structure of a classical jadal treatise.

Guided Path
1
Locate the main entry

2
Examine sub-entries under al-jadal
Look at entries like 'al-jadal, al-jidal' – the index may differentiate between dialectic and disputation. Notice that many sub-entries like 'question of objection' and 'tricks and fallacies' are further down the list.
Sub-entries show the specific aspects of the main topic the author addresses.
3
Identify key distinctions
The index lists pairs like 'Distinction between evidence and indicator' and 'Distinction between limit (hadd) and definition (ta'rif)'. These highlight important conceptual boundaries in jadal.
Such distinctions are foundational for proper argument analysis in Islamic logic.
4
Note the presence of 'tricks and fallacies'
The entry 'Tricks and fallacies in dialectic' shows that the author also discusses errors and deceptive arguments. This indicates the book covers both valid and invalid reasoning.
Knowing fallacies is as crucial as knowing valid forms in jadal training.

D) It summarizes the entire book in a few paragraphs.

Key Takeaway
An index of jadal terms reveals the conceptual structure of the discipline, highlighting key topics and their relationships through entries and page ranges.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Navigating an Usul al-Fiqh Index
Index of usuli rules and issues with page numbers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to locate key usuli issues and the positions of major imams in a structured index.

Core Idea
An index is a roadmap to a book's arguments; mastering it is a key academic skill.

This passage is an index from a work on usul al-fiqh, listing rules and issues with page numbers. It shows positions of imams like Malik, Shafi'i, Abu Hanifa, and Ahmad. Learning to navigate such indices allows you to quickly find the author's treatment of specific debates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heading structure
Notice the heading 'سادسا : فهرس القواعد والمسائل الأصولية' which introduces the index. The entries are grouped by topic, often with page numbers following.
2
Scan for imam names
Look for names like 'مالك', 'الشافعي', 'أبو حنيفة', 'أحمد'. Each imam's position is stated in a few words, e.g., 'عند مالك السنة مثل ذلك'.
3
Interpret abbreviated positions
Many entries are compressed: e.g., 'حجية خبر الواحد' means the authority of the solitary report. The page numbers indicate where in the book the discussion occurs.
Page numbers are in the original text; you may need to refer to the actual book.
4
Summarize a specific entry
Pick an entry (e.g., 'الإباحة، هل هي تكليف أم لا؟') and deduce the issue: Is permissibility a legal obligation? The index shows it is debated.

Commentary
This passage is a front matter index (فهرس) listing the rules and issues (القواعد والمسائل الأصولية) discussed in the book 'Jadal Usuliyyin'. It serves as a table of contents, organizing topics in usul al-fiqh with page references. The index begins with a heading indicating it is the sixth section. The entries cover a wide range of usuli topics: the nature of permissibility (الإباحة) as a legal obligation, the impossibility of impossible obligations, the modes of obligation (wajib kifaya, wajib mukhayyar), the sources of law (Book, Sunnah, and their indications), the implications of command forms, the authority of solitary reports (khabar al-wahid), the concepts (mafahim) of address (dilalat al-khitab), and various principles of interpretation. The index also includes positions of specific imams like Malik, al-Shafi'i, Abu Hanifa, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal. The page numbers scattered throughout indicate where each topic is discussed in the main text. This index provides an overview of the key debates in usul al-fiqh, particularly those relevant to dialectical argumentation (jadal) among jurists.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Debates on Obligation and Permissibility
Index of usuli rules and issues with page numbers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the different views on permissibility (ibaha) as a legal obligation and the modes of obligation (wajib kifaya and mukhayyar) from an index.

Core Idea
Permissibility and obligation are foundational concepts with nuanced disagreements among usulis.

The index opens with permissibility: 'هل هي تكليف أم لا؟' (Is it a legal obligation?). It then discusses modes of obligation: collective duty (wajib kifaya) and elective obligatory (wajib mukhayyar). These debates shape legal theory. Understanding them from an index entry prepares you for deeper study.

Guided Path
1
Locate the first entry
The index starts with 'الإباحة، هل هي تكليف أم لا؟'. This asks whether permissibility is a form of legal obligation (taklif).
2
Interpret the question
The question implies a disagreement: some usulis regard permissibility as a request not to act, thus not a taklif; others consider it a command to allow, thus a taklif.
3
Find the entry on obligation
Look for 'الوجوب' in the index. The entry 'كيفية الوجوب في الواجب على الكفاية' discusses the mode of obligation in collective duties.
4
Analyze the elective obligatory
The entry 'الواجب في الواجب المخير واحد لا يقبل التعيين وقال المعتزلة يجب الجميع' states that the obligatory in an elective duty is one unspecified act, but the Mu'tazila say all options are obligatory.
5
Relate to other entries
Other entries like 'اقتضاء صيغة الأمر' discuss whether the command form implies obligation, connecting to the nature of obligation.

Commentary
This passage is a front matter index (فهرس) listing the rules and issues (القواعد والمسائل الأصولية) discussed in the book 'Jadal Usuliyyin'. It serves as a table of contents, organizing topics in usul al-fiqh with page references. The index begins with a heading indicating it is the sixth section. The entries cover a wide range of usuli topics: the nature of permissibility (الإباحة) as a legal obligation, the impossibility of impossible obligations, the modes of obligation (wajib kifaya, wajib mukhayyar), the sources of law (Book, Sunnah, and their indications), the implications of command forms, the authority of solitary reports (khabar al-wahid), the concepts (mafahim) of address (dilalat al-khitab), and various principles of interpretation. The index also includes positions of specific imams like Malik, al-Shafi'i, Abu Hanifa, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal. The page numbers scattered throughout indicate where each topic is discussed in the main text. This index provides an overview of the key debates in usul al-fiqh, particularly those relevant to dialectical argumentation (jadal) among jurists.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Authority of Solitary Reports and Concepts
Index of usuli rules and issues with page numbers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Shafi'i, and the majority on the authority of solitary reports and concepts (mafahim) from an index.

Core Idea
The acceptance of solitary reports and concepts (mafahim) is a major point of divergence in usul.

The index lists key debates on khabar al-wahid and daleel al-khitab. Abu Hanifa rejects many concepts; Shafi'i uses them; Ahmad accepts weak hadiths. This lesson maps these positions using the index entries.

Guided Path
1
Find entries on solitary report
Locate 'حجية خبر الواحد' and 'خبر الواحد المخالف للقياس'. These entries discuss the authority of solitary reports and conditions for acceptance.
2
Note conditions for acceptance
For example, 'لا يقبل خبر الواحد فيا تعم به البلوى عند أبي حنيفة' means Abu Hanifa does not accept solitary reports in matters of general necessity. Another entry says 'خبر الواحد المخالف للقياس، لا يؤخذ به عند أبي حنيفة'.
3
Find 'دليل الخطاب' and concepts
The entry 'دليل الخطاب حجة عند جمهور الفقهاء والمتكلمين ما عدا مفهوم اللقب' shows the majority view. It also states Abu Hanifa and Zahiris denied all concepts.
4
Identify specific concepts
Look for 'مفهوم الشرط والصفة لا اعتبار له عند أبي حنيفة' and 'مفهوم الغاية حجة عند الحنفية'. This shows the Hanafi position varies by concept type.
5
Compare with other imams
Note Imam Ahmad's position: he takes mursal and weak hadith if no contradicting report exists, giving them precedence over analogy.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
Default Rulings: Al-Ibaha and Al-Istishab
Foundational presumptions in legal theory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the default permissibility principle (ibaha) from the presumption of continuity (istishab) and identify when istishab is abandoned according to the passage.

Core Idea
Everything is permissible unless proven otherwise, and that default remains until evidence changes it.

In usul al-fiqh, two foundational principles govern rulings in the absence of evidence: al-ibaha (default permissibility) and al-istishab (presumption of continuity). This lesson clarifies their meanings and limits as listed in the source.

Guided Path
1
Locate the phrase for al-ibaha
Find 'أصل الأشياء على الإباحة' in the Arabic list. This states the default ruling that things are permissible unless there is proof to the contrary.
2
Understand the scope of ibaha
This principle applies to all things (ashya') and is a key starting point for legal reasoning. Remember it is a default, not a final ruling.
3
Find the entry for istishab
Look for 'يترك العمل بالاستصحاب إذا ورد الدليل بحكم من الشرع' which explains that istishab is abandoned when any legal proof appears, whether textual or ijtihadi.
Istishab is the continuation of a presumed ruling; it is overridden by evidence.
4
Contrast the two principles
Ibaha is a default permission, while istishab is a presumption of continuity. Both are provisional until evidence arises, but istishab explicitly mentions being left when proof comes.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أصل الأشياء على الإباحة
إنكار الإمام الشافعي الاحتجاج بالاستحسان
إنكار الإمام الشافعي الاحتجاج بعمل أهل المدينة
إنكار الإمام الشافعي الاحتجاج بالمصالح المرسلة
حجية الأدلة العقلية
الحكم بسد الذرائع معتبر عند مالك وأحمد
شرع من قبلنا هو شرع لنا ما لم يرد في شريعتنا ما ينص صراحة على إلغائه
عمل أهل المدينة معتبر عند الإمام مالك
العمل بالمصالح المرسلة معتبر عند الإمام مالك
قول الصحابي هل هو حجة؟
قول الصحابي معتبر عند مالك إذا صح سنده وكان من الأعلام
لجوء أبي حنيفة إلى العمل بأقوال الصحابة إذا لم يجد نصا من الكتاب أو السنة
ما لا يعين العقل فيه قبحا ولا حسنا هل هو على الحظر أم على الإباحة؟
مذهب الصحابي على خلاف العموم مخصص له عند أبي حنيفة
يترك العمل بالاستصحاب إذا ورد الدليل بحكم من الشرع في المسالة سواء كان هذا الدليل لفظا من الشارع أو دليلا اجتهاديا كالقياس أو غيره
الاجتهاد
الاختلاف بسبب تباين الرأي والاجتهاد
الاختلاف بسبب التباين في فهم دلالات القرآن
الاختلاف بسبب تعارض ظواهر النصوص
اختلاف الصحابة بسبب تفاوتهم في السماع من الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم والتحري في الأخذ بالسنة والاجتهاد في فهمها
الأدلة ليست كلها في مرتبة واحدة فبعضها أقوى من بعض في الحجية فيكون أحق بالتقديم عليه في النظر والاستدلال
إذا لم يجد الإمام أحمد نصا في المسالة انتقل إلى فتوى الصحابة
الفرق بعلة الحكم
العمل بالظن واجب إذا كان عن أمارة مقتضية للحكم
المصيب في مسائل الاجتهاد واحد والمخطئ معذور مأجور
هل الأصول هي الحقائق أنفسها أم العلم بها؟
هل يجوز أن يكون للعلم أكثر من موضوع واحد أم لا؟
التعارض والترجيح
الأخذ بالقياس وترك الاستحسان عندما تظهر إلى ذلك حاجة عند أبي حنيفة
إذا اختلف الصحابة تخير الإمام أحمد من أقوالهم أقربها إلى الكتاب والسنة ولم يخرج عن أقوالهم فإن لم يتضح له الأقرب إلى الكتاب والسنة حكى الخلاف ولم يجزم بقول منها
إذا تعارض الخبر مع الآية على وجه لا يمكن الجمع بينهما يكون الأخذ بالآية أولى لأنها معلومة
إذا تكافأت الأحاديث فأصحها إسنادا أولاها عند الشافعي
إذا كان الجمع بين الآيتين ممكنا فلا يجوز أن نصير إلى النسخ
الآية التي قصد بها بيان الحكم المختلف فيه أولى من الآية التي لم يقصد بها ذلك
ترجيح المانع على المقتضي
تقديم القياس على قول الصحابي
الجمع بين الآيتين واستعمالهما أولى من إسقاط إحداهما
رد القياس إذا عارض النص
لا يجوز معارضة نص الكتاب بالقياس ولا بغيره من الأدلة
يتقدم القياس الجلي على خبر الواحد المعارض له عند أبي حنيفة
The origin of things is permissibility
Imam al-Shafi'i's rejection of argument by istihsan
Imam al-Shafi'i's rejection of argument by the practice of the people of Medina
Imam al-Shafi'i's rejection of argument by masalih mursala
Authority of rational evidences
Ruling by blocking the means is considered by Malik and Ahmad
Law of those before us is law for us as long as nothing in our law explicitly abrogates it
The practice of the people of Medina is considered by Imam Malik
Working with masalih mursala is considered by Imam Malik
Is the statement of a companion a proof?
The statement of a companion is considered by Malik if its chain is authentic and it is from the prominent ones
Abu Hanifa's resort to the statements of companions when he finds no text from Book or Sunna
What the intellect does not determine as ugly or good: is it prohibition or permissibility?
The doctrine of a companion contrary to the general is a specification of it according to Abu Hanifa
One leaves working with istishab if a proof by a ruling of the Law comes in the matter, whether that proof is a verbal text from the Lawgiver or an ijtihadi proof like qiyas or other
Ijtihad
Disagreement due to difference of opinion and ijtihad
Disagreement due to difference in understanding the implications of the Qur'an
Disagreement due to conflict of apparent meanings of texts
Disagreement of the companions due to their variation in hearing from the Prophet (peace be upon him) and thoroughness in taking the Sunna and ijtihad in understanding it
All evidences are not in one rank; some are stronger than others in authority, so they are more deserving of precedence in consideration and inference
If Imam Ahmad finds no text in a matter, he turns to the fatwa of the companions
The difference in the 'illa of the ruling
Working with probability is obligatory if it is based on an indicator that necessitates the ruling
The one who hits the mark in matters of ijtihad is one, and the one who errs is excused and rewarded
Are the principles the realities themselves or knowledge of them?
Is it permissible for knowledge to have more than one subject or not?
Conflict and preponderance
Taking qiyas and leaving istihsan when need appears for that according to Abu Hanifa
If the companions disagreed, Imam Ahmad chooses from their statements the closest to Book and Sunna and does not go beyond their statements; if the closest to Book and Sunna is not clear to him, he relates the disagreement and does not decide on any statement
If the hadith conflicts with the verse in a way that combination is impossible, then taking the verse is preferable because it is known
If the hadiths are equal, the one with the most authentic chain is the most deserving according to al-Shafi'i
If combination between two verses is possible, then it is not permissible to resort to abrogation
The verse that intends to clarify the ruling in dispute is more deserving than the verse that did not intend that
Preponderance of the preventing factor over the requiring factor
Preferring qiyas over the statement of a companion
Combining the two verses and using them is more deserving than dropping one of them
Rejecting qiyas if it conflicts with a text
It is not permissible to oppose the text of the Book by qiyas or any other evidence
Clear qiyas takes precedence over a single report that conflicts with it according to Abu Hanifa
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage is a list of topics or summary of key debated principles in usul al-fiqh and the positions of major imams (Abu Hanifa, al-Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad). It likely serves as a table of contents or index for a work on jadal (dialectical debate) among legal theorists. The items cover a wide range of issues: the default permissibility of things, rejection of istihsan by al-Shafi'i, rejection of Medinan practice and masalih mursala, the authority of rational evidence, blocking the means (sadd al-dhara'i') according to Malik and Ahmad, the law of previous prophets, the practice of Medinans as proof, companion statements and their authority, istishab, ijtihad, causes of disagreement, conflict of evidences, and rules for preference (tarjih). Each point is a distinct doctrine or methodological principle that would be discussed and debated. Students should parse each term and identify the associated imam and the significance of the principle in legal theory. For example, 'istihsan' is rejected by al-Shafi'i but used by Abu Hanifa. The passage is a concise overview of the subject matter of the book.
