D) Only when qiyas is used

Key Takeaway
The default permissibility of things (ibaha) is the starting point, and the presumption of continuity (istishab) holds until any evidence overrides it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify a scenario in fiqh where the principle of ibaha would apply and explain why.
?
Given a situation where a person's ritual purity is in doubt, determine whether istishab applies and whether it can be overridden.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Controversial Sources: Istihsan, Masalih Mursala, and Sadd al-Dhara'i'
Debated extra-textual sources and imam positions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which imams accepted or rejected istihsan, masalih mursala, and sadd al-dhara'i', and explain the basic meaning of each source.

Core Idea
Not all extra-textual sources are accepted by all imams; knowing their positions is essential for understanding ijtihad.

Three important yet debated extra-textual sources are istihsan (juristic preference), masalih mursala (unrestricted public interest), and sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking means). This lesson helps you parse the passage and associate each principle with the imams who accepted or rejected them.

Guided Path
1
Find the phrase about istihsan
Locate 'إنكار الإمام الشافعي الاحتجاج بالاستحسان' which indicates al-Shafi'i rejected istihsan. Note also 'الأخذ بالقياس وترك الاستحسان عندما تظهر إلى ذلك حاجة عند أبي حنيفة' showing that Abu Hanifa would leave istihsan for qiyas when needed.
Istihsan is a departure from strict analogy for a stronger reason.
2
Find masalih mursala entries
Look for 'إنكار الإمام الشافعي الاحتجاج بالمصالح المرسلة' (rejection by al-Shafi'i) and 'العمل بالمصالح المرسلة معتبر عند الإمام مالك' (acceptance by Malik).
Masalih mursala are public interests not explicitly mentioned in texts.
3
Find sadd al-dhara'i' entry
Find 'الحكم بسد الذرائع معتبر عند مالك وأحمد' which states that blocking the means is considered by Malik and Ahmad.
This principle prevents actions that may lead to prohibited outcomes.
4
Compare the acceptance and rejection patterns
Notice that al-Shafi'i rejects both istihsan and masalih mursala, while Malik accepts both and also sadd al-dhara'i'. Abu Hanifa uses istihsan conditionally. Ahmad accepts sadd al-dhara'i'.
This shows methodological differences among the imams.

إذا لم يجد الإمام أحمد نصا في المسالة انتقل إلى فتوى الصحابة
الفرق بعلة الحكم
العمل بالظن واجب إذا كان عن أمارة مقتضية للحكم

هل الأصول هي الحقائق أنفسها أم العلم بها؟
هل يجوز أن يكون للعلم أكثر من موضوع واحد أم لا؟

الأخذ بالقياس وترك الاستحسان عندما تظهر إلى ذلك حاجة عند أبي حنيفة
إذا اختلف الصحابة تخير الإمام أحمد من أقوالهم أقربها إلى الكتاب والسنة ولم يخرج عن أقوالهم فإن لم يتضح له الأقرب إلى الكتاب والسنة حكى الخلاف ولم يجزم بقول منها
إذا تعارض الخبر مع الآية على وجه لا يمكن الجمع بينهما يكون الأخذ بالآية أولى لأنها معلومة
إذا تكافأت الأحاديث فأصحها إسنادا أولاها عند الشافعي
إذا كان الجمع بين الآيتين ممكنا فلا يجوز أن نصير إلى النسخ
الآية التي قصد بها بيان الحكم المختلف فيه أولى من الآية التي لم يقصد بها ذلك
ترجيح المانع على المقتضي
تقديم القياس على قول الصحابي
الجمع بين الآيتين واستعمالهما أولى من إسقاط إحداهما
رد القياس إذا عارض النص

يتقدم القياس الجلي على خبر الواحد المعارض له عند أبي حنيفة

Imam al-Shafi'i's rejection of argument by istihsan

Imam al-Shafi'i's rejection of argument by masalih mursala

Ruling by blocking the means is considered by Malik and Ahmad
Law of those before us is law for us as long as nothing in our law explicitly abrogates it
The practice of the people of Medina is considered by Imam Malik
Working with masalih mursala is considered by Imam Malik

The statement of a companion is considered by Malik if its chain is authentic and it is from the prominent ones
Abu Hanifa's resort to the statements of companions when he finds no text from Book or Sunna
What the intellect does not determine as ugly or good: is it prohibition or permissibility?
The doctrine of a companion contrary to the general is a specification of it according to Abu Hanifa
One leaves working with istishab if a proof by a ruling of the Law comes in the matter, whether that proof is a verbal text from the Lawgiver or an ijtihadi proof like qiyas or other
Ijtihad
Disagreement due to difference of opinion and ijtihad
Disagreement due to difference in understanding the implications of the Qur'an
Disagreement due to conflict of apparent meanings of texts
Disagreement of the companions due to their variation in hearing from the Prophet (peace be upon him) and thoroughness in taking the Sunna and ijtihad in understanding it

If Imam Ahmad finds no text in a matter, he turns to the fatwa of the companions
The difference in the 'illa of the ruling
Working with probability is obligatory if it is based on an indicator that necessitates the ruling
The one who hits the mark in matters of ijtihad is one, and the one who errs is excused and rewarded
Are the principles the realities themselves or knowledge of them?
Is it permissible for knowledge to have more than one subject or not?
Conflict and preponderance
Taking qiyas and leaving istihsan when need appears for that according to Abu Hanifa
If the companions disagreed, Imam Ahmad chooses from their statements the closest to Book and Sunna and does not go beyond their statements; if the closest to Book and Sunna is not clear to him, he relates the disagreement and does not decide on any statement
If the hadith conflicts with the verse in a way that combination is impossible, then taking the verse is preferable because it is known
If the hadiths are equal, the one with the most authentic chain is the most deserving according to al-Shafi'i
If combination between two verses is possible, then it is not permissible to resort to abrogation
The verse that intends to clarify the ruling in dispute is more deserving than the verse that did not intend that
Preponderance of the preventing factor over the requiring factor
Preferring qiyas over the statement of a companion
Combining the two verses and using them is more deserving than dropping one of them
Rejecting qiyas if it conflicts with a text
It is not permissible to oppose the text of the Book by qiyas or any other evidence
Clear qiyas takes precedence over a single report that conflicts with it according to Abu Hanifa

Commentary
This passage is a list of topics or summary of key debated principles in usul al-fiqh and the positions of major imams (Abu Hanifa, al-Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad). It likely serves as a table of contents or index for a work on jadal (dialectical debate) among legal theorists. The items cover a wide range of issues: the default permissibility of things, rejection of istihsan by al-Shafi'i, rejection of Medinan practice and masalih mursala, the authority of rational evidence, blocking the means (sadd al-dhara'i') according to Malik and Ahmad, the law of previous prophets, the practice of Medinans as proof, companion statements and their authority, istishab, ijtihad, causes of disagreement, conflict of evidences, and rules for preference (tarjih). Each point is a distinct doctrine or methodological principle that would be discussed and debated. Students should parse each term and identify the associated imam and the significance of the principle in legal theory. For example, 'istihsan' is rejected by al-Shafi'i but used by Abu Hanifa. The passage is a concise overview of the subject matter of the book.

Authority of Companion Statements and Previous Laws
Authority of secondary sources in legal reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the authority of companion statements (qawl al-sahabi) and previous prophetic laws (shar' man qablana) according to the imams mentioned in the passage.

Core Idea
Companion statements and earlier revelations are sources for some imams but not all, and their use is conditional.

Two debated sources in usul al-fiqh are the statements of the Prophet's companions and the laws of previous prophets. The passage lists specific imams and their approaches to these sources, which we will parse in this lesson.

Guided Path
1
Locate the entries about companion statements
Find 'قول الصحابي هل هو حجة؟' which poses the question of authority. Then see 'قول الصحابي معتبر عند مالك إذا صح سنده وكان من الأعلام' – Malik accepts if chain is authentic and from prominent companions. Also find 'لجوء أبي حنيفة إلى العمل بأقوال الصحابة إذا لم يجد نصا من الكتاب أو السنة' – Abu Hanifa resorts to companion statements when no text from Quran/Sunnah.
Also note 'مذهب الصحابي على خلاف العموم مخصص له عند أبي حنيفة' – companion opinion contrary to general rule is a specification for Abu Hanifa.
2
Find the entry about previous laws
Look for 'شرع من قبلنا هو شرع لنا ما لم يرد في شريعتنا ما ينص صراحة على إلغائه' which states that laws of previous prophets are binding unless explicitly abrogated by Islamic law.
This is a general principle, not attributed to a specific imam in this list.
3
Identify imam-specific conditions
Malik conditions acceptance on authentic chain and prominent companion. Abu Hanifa uses them only in the absence of Quran/Sunnah texts. Ahmad's approach is not listed here for companion statements, but he used fatwas of companions when no text (see later entry).
The passage gives a nuanced picture of how different imams relied on these sources.

Introduction and Front Matter

Ijtihad and Causes of Disagreement
Sources of disagreement in legal reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the main causes of disagreement among the companions and imams as mentioned in this passage.

Core Idea
Disagreement in ijtihad arises from differences in hearing, understanding, and methodological approaches.

The passage lists several reasons why the companions and later jurists disagreed on legal rulings. This lesson focuses on those causes, which are essential for understanding the diversity of opinions in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Locate the causes of disagreement
Find the lines starting with 'الاختلاف' and 'اختلاف الصحابة'. They list causes: difference of opinion and ijtihad, difference in understanding Qur'anic implications, conflict of textual apparent meanings, and companions' variation in hearing from the Prophet and thoroughness in taking the Sunna.
These are general causes; note the last one is specific to companions.
2
Identify the principle about evidence strength
The line 'الأدلة ليست كلها في مرتبة واحدة' states that evidences are not all of the same rank; some are stronger and thus deserve precedence.
This contributes to disagreement when jurists rank evidences differently.
3
Relate causes to imam methodology
Later lines show how imams handled disagreement: e.g., Ahmad chose the closest to Quran and Sunnah; if unclear, he related the disagreement without deciding.
This shows that methodology in handling disagreement also varies.

لجوء أبي حنيفة إلى العمل بأقوال الصحابة إذا لم يجد نصا من الكتاب أو السنة
ما لا يعين العقل فيه قبحا ولا حسنا هل هو على الحظر أم على الإباحة؟
مذهب الصحابي على خلاف العموم مخصص له عند أبي حنيفة
يترك العمل بالاستصحاب إذا ورد الدليل بحكم من الشرع في المسالة سواء كان هذا الدليل لفظا من الشارع أو دليلا اجتهاديا كالقياس أو غيره
الاجتهاد
الاختلاف بسبب تباين الرأي والاجتهاد
الاختلاف بسبب التباين في فهم دلالات القرآن
الاختلاف بسبب تعارض ظواهر النصوص
اختلاف الصحابة بسبب تفاوتهم في السماع من الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم والتحري في الأخذ بالسنة والاجتهاد في فهمها
الأدلة ليست كلها في مرتبة واحدة فبعضها أقوى من بعض في الحجية فيكون أحق بالتقديم عليه في النظر والاستدلال
إذا لم يجد الإمام أحمد نصا في المسالة انتقل إلى فتوى الصحابة
الفرق بعلة الحكم
العمل بالظن واجب إذا كان عن أمارة مقتضية للحكم
المصيب في مسائل الاجتهاد واحد والمخطئ معذور مأجور
هل الأصول هي الحقائق أنفسها أم العلم بها؟
هل يجوز أن يكون للعلم أكثر من موضوع واحد أم لا؟
التعارض والترجيح
الأخذ بالقياس وترك الاستحسان عندما تظهر إلى ذلك حاجة عند أبي حنيفة
إذا اختلف الصحابة تخير الإمام أحمد من أقوالهم أقربها إلى الكتاب والسنة ولم يخرج عن أقوالهم فإن لم يتضح له الأقرب إلى الكتاب والسنة حكى الخلاف ولم يجزم بقول منها
إذا تعارض الخبر مع الآية على وجه لا يمكن الجمع بينهما يكون الأخذ بالآية أولى لأنها معلومة
إذا تكافأت الأحاديث فأصحها إسنادا أولاها عند الشافعي
إذا كان الجمع بين الآيتين ممكنا فلا يجوز أن نصير إلى النسخ
الآية التي قصد بها بيان الحكم المختلف فيه أولى من الآية التي لم يقصد بها ذلك
ترجيح المانع على المقتضي
تقديم القياس على قول الصحابي
الجمع بين الآيتين واستعمالهما أولى من إسقاط إحداهما
رد القياس إذا عارض النص
لا يجوز معارضة نص الكتاب بالقياس ولا بغيره من الأدلة
يتقدم القياس الجلي على خبر الواحد المعارض له عند أبي حنيفة
The origin of things is permissibility
Imam al-Shafi'i's rejection of argument by istihsan
Imam al-Shafi'i's rejection of argument by the practice of the people of Medina
Imam al-Shafi'i's rejection of argument by masalih mursala
Authority of rational evidences
Ruling by blocking the means is considered by Malik and Ahmad
Law of those before us is law for us as long as nothing in our law explicitly abrogates it
The practice of the people of Medina is considered by Imam Malik
Working with masalih mursala is considered by Imam Malik
Is the statement of a companion a proof?
The statement of a companion is considered by Malik if its chain is authentic and it is from the prominent ones
Abu Hanifa's resort to the statements of companions when he finds no text from Book or Sunna
What the intellect does not determine as ugly or good: is it prohibition or permissibility?
The doctrine of a companion contrary to the general is a specification of it according to Abu Hanifa
One leaves working with istishab if a proof by a ruling of the Law comes in the matter, whether that proof is a verbal text from the Lawgiver or an ijtihadi proof like qiyas or other
Ijtihad
Disagreement due to difference of opinion and ijtihad
Disagreement due to difference in understanding the implications of the Qur'an
Disagreement due to conflict of apparent meanings of texts
Disagreement of the companions due to their variation in hearing from the Prophet (peace be upon him) and thoroughness in taking the Sunna and ijtihad in understanding it
All evidences are not in one rank; some are stronger than others in authority, so they are more deserving of precedence in consideration and inference
If Imam Ahmad finds no text in a matter, he turns to the fatwa of the companions
The difference in the 'illa of the ruling
Working with probability is obligatory if it is based on an indicator that necessitates the ruling
The one who hits the mark in matters of ijtihad is one, and the one who errs is excused and rewarded
Are the principles the realities themselves or knowledge of them?
Is it permissible for knowledge to have more than one subject or not?
Conflict and preponderance
Taking qiyas and leaving istihsan when need appears for that according to Abu Hanifa
If the companions disagreed, Imam Ahmad chooses from their statements the closest to Book and Sunna and does not go beyond their statements; if the closest to Book and Sunna is not clear to him, he relates the disagreement and does not decide on any statement
If the hadith conflicts with the verse in a way that combination is impossible, then taking the verse is preferable because it is known
If the hadiths are equal, the one with the most authentic chain is the most deserving according to al-Shafi'i
If combination between two verses is possible, then it is not permissible to resort to abrogation
The verse that intends to clarify the ruling in dispute is more deserving than the verse that did not intend that
Preponderance of the preventing factor over the requiring factor
Preferring qiyas over the statement of a companion
Combining the two verses and using them is more deserving than dropping one of them
Rejecting qiyas if it conflicts with a text
It is not permissible to oppose the text of the Book by qiyas or any other evidence
Clear qiyas takes precedence over a single report that conflicts with it according to Abu Hanifa
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage is a list of topics or summary of key debated principles in usul al-fiqh and the positions of major imams (Abu Hanifa, al-Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad). It likely serves as a table of contents or index for a work on jadal (dialectical debate) among legal theorists. The items cover a wide range of issues: the default permissibility of things, rejection of istihsan by al-Shafi'i, rejection of Medinan practice and masalih mursala, the authority of rational evidence, blocking the means (sadd al-dhara'i') according to Malik and Ahmad, the law of previous prophets, the practice of Medinans as proof, companion statements and their authority, istishab, ijtihad, causes of disagreement, conflict of evidences, and rules for preference (tarjih). Each point is a distinct doctrine or methodological principle that would be discussed and debated. Students should parse each term and identify the associated imam and the significance of the principle in legal theory. For example, 'istihsan' is rejected by al-Shafi'i but used by Abu Hanifa. The passage is a concise overview of the subject matter of the book.

المصالح المرسلة
سد الذرائع
شرع من قبلنا
قول الصحابي

According to the passage, which of the following is a cause of disagreement among the companions?
A) They intentionally differed to expand the law

Key Takeaway
Disagreement in ijtihad stems from differences in understanding, methodology, and access to texts, and is considered a natural part of Islamic legal reasoning.

Introduction and Front Matter
advanced
7 min
Principles of Tarjih (Preferencing) When Evidences Conflict
Rules for preferring evidences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply several rules for preferring one evidence over another when they conflict, as stated in this passage.

Core Idea
When evidences conflict, established rules of tarjih determine which takes precedence, ensuring systematic resolution.

The passage contains numerous rules for tarjih (preponderance) when evidences appear to conflict. These rules are essential for a jurist to prioritize evidence. This lesson organizes and explains these rules.

Guided Path
1
List the tarjih rules from the passage
Scan the passage for phrases like 'أولى', 'يتقدم', 'تقديم', 'ترجيح'. Extract rules such as: verse over hadith if combination impossible, most authentic hadith over weaker, combination over abrogation, verse intending clarification over general verse, preventing factor over requiring factor, qiyas over companion statement, clear qiyas over solitary report, etc.
Note which rules are attributed to specific imams (e.g., al-Shafi'i said most authentic chain is most deserving).
2
Categorize the rules
Group rules by type: textual priority (verse vs hadith), authenticity priority (chain strength), methodological priority (qiyas over companion statement, clear qiyas over solitary report), and logical priority (preventing factor over requiring).
3
Identify imam-specific rules
Some rules are explicitly linked to an imam: 'إذا تكافأت الأحاديث فأصحها إسنادا أولاها عند الشافعي' and 'يتقدم القياس الجلي على خبر الواحد المعارض له عند أبي حنيفة'.
This shows that tarjih rules can be school-specific.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Navigating Fiqh Issues Through Jadal
Subject index of fiqh issues for jadal debate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to navigate a jadal-oriented index of fiqh issues and identify how each question is framed for dialectical debate.

Core Idea
Jadal in fiqh starts with a clearly framed yes/no question.

This index presents a list of fiqh questions that are typically debated using the dialectical method (jadal) in usul al-fiqh. Rather than providing answers, the index serves as a roadmap for where jadal is applied. Understanding how these questions are structured helps you see the logical entry points for dialectical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main categories
The index is divided into three sections: purification (ṭahāra), prayer (ṣalāh), and zakāt. Note the headings and the range of issues under each.
2
Observe the question format
Each issue is phrased as a yes/no or either/or question (e.g., 'هل يجب؟', 'هل يجوز؟'). This is the typical starting point for jadal, where disputants take opposing sides.
3
Connect to jadal methodology
In jadal, the disputants hold opposing positions on such questions. The index shows the breadth of topics where dialectical arguments are relevant – from tahara details to prayer and zakat.
4
Recognize the scope
The index covers detailed fiqh issues, from wudu with nabidh to the time for 'isha' to zakat on horses. This demonstrates that jadal is not limited to abstract usul principles but is applied to specific furu' rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سابعا : فهرس الأحكام والمسائل الفقهية
الجدل

الطهارة -
- إزالة النجاسة بغير الماء
- الاستجمار ، هل يعتبر فيه العدد؟
- التقاء الختانين، هل يوجب الغسل؟
- الترتيب في الوضوء، هل هو واجب؟
- التيمم هل يجب فيه مسح اليدين إلى المرفقين؟
- الثوب، هل يجب غسله من المني؟
- جلد الكلب، هل يطهر بالدباغ؟
- جلد الكلب، هل يطهر بالذكاة؟
- جلد الميتة، هل يطهر بالدباغ؟
- جواز التيمم بالحصى والحجارة
- الحامل، هل تحيض أم لا؟
- الخارج من غير السبيلين، هل ينقض الوضوء؟
- خروج الدم هل يوجب الوضوء؟
- الزوجة، هل يجوز لزوجها أن يغسلها إذا ماتت؟
- سؤر السباع، هل هو نجس؟
- الشعر، هل ينجس بالموت؟
- غسل الإناء من ولوغ الخنزير، هل هو واجب؟
- غسل الجنابة هل يجب فيه المضمضة والاستنشاق؟
- القهقهة في الصلاة، هل تنقض الوضوء؟
- القيء، هل يبطل الوضوء؟
- مس المحدث، هل يجوز له المصحف؟
- مس النساء، هل ينقض الوضوء؟
- مسح الرأس في الوضوء، هل يسن تكراره؟
- مسح الرأس في الوضوء، هل الواجب فيه هو الربع؟
- مسح الرأس في الوضوء، هل يجب الاستيعاب فيه؟
- المني، هل هو طاهر أم نجس؟
- النجاسة، هل يجوز إزالتها بالخل؟
- الموالاة في الوضوء، هل هي شرط في صحته؟
- الموالاة، هل هي شرط في الطهارة؟
- نقض المرأة شعر رأسها إذا اغتسلت
- النية، هل هي واجبة في الطهارة؟
- وجوب النية في أول العبادة، ولا يجب تجديدها
- الوضوء، هل يجوز بالنبيذ؟
- الوضوء، هل يجب مما مست النار؟
- الوضوء، هل يفتقر إلى النية؟

الصلاة -
- الإحرام في الصلاة بقوله «الله الأكبر»، هل يجوز؟
- تارك الصلاة متعمدا هل هو مطالب بقضائها وجوبًا؟
- تحديد وقت العشاء
- رفع اليدين في تكبيرة الإحرام، هل هو إلى حذو المنكبين أم إلى حيال الأذنين؟
- سجود التلاوة، هل هو واجب؟
- سجود السهو في النقصان هل يكون قبل السلام أم بعده؟
- هل يحكم ببلوغ الغلام في السادسة عشرة؟ أم في الثامنة عشرة؟
- الصلاة على القبر، هل تجوز؟
- الصلاة في الدار المغصوبة، هل تصح؟
- الصلاة في المقبرة والحمام، هل تصح؟
- فضيلة إتيان الجمعة هل لا تكون إلا في أول النهار؟
- الصلاة، هل تجب على المأموم؟
- قراءة الفاتحة في الصلاة، هل تجب على المأموم؟
- قراءة المأموم خلف الإمام في الصلاة
- قصر الصلاة في ثلاثة أميال، هل يجوز؟
- القيام في الصلاة هل يجب على المصلي في السفينة؟
- الوتر، هل هو واجب؟

الزكاة -
- استئناف الفريضة في زكاة الإبل
- إناث الخيل هل تجب فيها الزكاة؟
- الخيل هل تجب فيها زكاة العين؟
- زكاة الفطر هل تجب بغروب شمس آخر يوم من رمضان أم بطلوع الفجر من أول يوم من شوال؟
Seventh: Index of fiqh rulings and issues
Dialectic (jadal)

Purification:
- Removing impurity with something other than water
- Istijmar (cleansing with stones), does number matter?

- The one who deliberately abandons prayer, is he required to make it up obligatorily?

- The follower's recitation behind the imam in prayer
- Shortening prayer at three miles, is it permissible?
- Standing in prayer, is it obligatory for the one praying on a ship?
- Witr prayer, is it obligatory?

- Restarting the obligation in zakat of camels
- Female horses, is zakat due on them?
- Horses, is zakat of 'ayn due on them?
- Zakat al-fiṭr, is it obligatory by sunset of the last day of Ramadan or by dawn of the first day of Shawwāl?

Commentary
This passage is an index of fiqh issues organized under the main categories of purification (ṭahāra), prayer (ṣalāh), and zakāh. It lists questions that are typically debated using the dialectical method (jadal) in uṣūl al-fiqh. The index shows the breadth of topics covered in the book 'Jadal Usuliyyin', indicating that the author applies jadal to detailed points of jurisprudence, from the minutiae of wuḍūʾ and ghusl to the rulings of prayer and zakāh. For each issue, the question is phrased in a yes/no or either/or format, which is characteristic of dialectical inquiry. This material serves as a reference for the reader to locate discussions of specific fiqh questions within the work.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Reading a Fihrist of Jurisprudential Issues for Jadal
A fihrist of fiqh questions to be debated in the work.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the structure and purpose of a fihrist of jurisprudential issues in a jadal work, and locate key debates under main fiqh headings.

Core Idea
A fihrist of masā’il is the skeleton of a jadal work: it shows the disputed questions to be resolved through structured debate.

This passage is not an argument but a roadmap. It lists the jurisprudential issues to be debated using jadal. As a student of Islamic logic and law, you need to understand how a jadal work is organized: the author first enumerates the points of contention under each fiqh chapter. This list tells you the scope of the dialectical arguments that follow. By parsing this fihrist, you will learn to recognize the typical structure of a jadal text and the types of questions suitable for dialectical treatment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main fiqh chapters
The list is organized under standard headings: purification (al-ṭahāra), prayer (al-ṣalāh), zakat, fasting (al-ṣawm), pilgrimage (al-ḥajj), and foods and drinks (al-aṭʿima wa al-ashriba). Notice each heading is followed by a series of questions.
Some chapters are separated by dashes and headings in the Arabic.
2
Note the question format
Each issue is phrased as a yes/no question with هل (hal) + verb, e.g., هل النية واجبة في الطهارة؟ (Is intention obligatory in purification?). This indicates a point of contention among jurists.
The questions are the topics for the dialectical arguments that follow later in the work.
3
Examine a sample question under each chapter
For purification, note questions about continuity (al-muwālāh), intention, and the permissibility of nabidh for ablution. For prayer, questions about takbīr, raising hands, and recitation. These are classic debates.
Think about why each question might be disputed between schools of law.
4
Recognize the non-exhaustive nature
This list is a selection of problematic points for dialectical treatment, not an exhaustive compilation. The author chooses issues that are suitable for the methods of jadal.
This is a common feature of jadal works: they focus on points of ikhtilāf that can be resolved through argumentation.
5
Link to the purpose of the work
The fihrist serves as a table of contents. The work will later present arguments for and against each issue following the rules of jadal (disputation). Understanding this list prepares you to follow the dialectical exchanges.
Each question will be taken up in order, with a defender and an objector.

Commentary
This passage is a fihrist (table of contents) listing the jurisprudential issues (masa'il) that will be debated in the work 'Jadal Usuliyyin'. The topics are organized under standard fiqh headings: purification (tahara), prayer (salah), zakat, fasting (sawm), pilgrimage (hajj), and foods and drinks. Each issue is phrased as a yes/no question (هل + verb) indicating a point of contention among jurists. The passage serves as a roadmap for the dialectical arguments (jadal) that follow. The author is presenting the scope of the work, which is to apply the methods of jadal (dialectical debate) to specific legal questions. The list includes classic debates such as whether intention is obligatory for purification, the permissibility of shortening prayer, the nisab of zakat, the conditions for fasting, and the penalties for hunting while in ihram. All examples are rooted in the Islamic legal tradition.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Navigating a Fihrist of Jadal Masa'il
Index of legal questions debated in jadal among usuliyyin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to parse a fihrist of jadal masa'il and identify the key fiqh domains and question patterns.

Core Idea
A fihrist of masa'il is a map of the debates; knowing the topics is half the argument.

This passage is not a continuous argument but an index—a list of legal questions that scholars debated through dialectical reasoning (jadal). In usul al-fiqh works, such tables of contents serve as a roadmap. Mastering the structure helps you anticipate the lines of argument in the main text. Let's learn how to read this fihrist like a seasoned faqih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Genre
Recognize that this is a fihrist (index). It lacks full argumentation—only short questions. This tells you it is a front-matter list, not a detailed discussion.
The absence of justifications and counterarguments confirms it's a table of contents.
2
Notice the Question Pattern
Most entries are yes/no questions beginning with 'هل' (is it...?). Some are brief legal problems. This format flags that each masa'la has two sides to argue.
For example: 'هل تثبت فيه الشفعة؟' (is the right of pre-emption established?)
3
Categorize by Fiqh Domain
Scan the list and group the questions by topic: marriage, divorce, inheritance, hudud, etc. This shows how jadal covers all branches of fiqh.
E.g., 'ملك اليمين' (right hand possession) belongs to family law.
4
Link to Legal Principles
Each masa'la relies on usul principles like qiyas (analogy), istihsan, or textual interpretation. For instance, the question about musaqat (contract of watering) analogizes from mudaraba.
Understanding the underlying principle helps you reconstruct the debate.

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter index (fihrist) listing numerous legal questions (masa'il) that are topics of dialectical debate (jadal) among usuliyyin (legal theorists). Each line presents a specific issue, typically framed as a yes/no question (هل...؟) or as a concise legal problem. The issues cover a wide range of fiqh topics: marriage (nikah), divorce (talaq), inheritance (mirath), hudud (penalties), kaffarat (expiation), etc. The presence of page numbers (omitted here) suggests this is a table of contents for a larger work. The student is expected to recognize these as typical points of contention in usul al-fiqh discussions, where the method of analogical reasoning (qiyas) and textual evidence (nusus) are applied. Each issue would be elaborated with proofs and counter-arguments in the main text.

شُفْعَة
فهرست
مسألة

Checkpoint
What is the primary function of the passage on pages 536-537 of Jadal Usuliyyin?
A) It provides detailed proofs for each legal issue.
B) It serves as a table of contents listing dialectical topics.
C) It defines the term 'jadal' for the first time.
D) It explains the methodology of qiyas.

Key Takeaway
A fihrist of masa'il is not the debate itself, but the skeleton; understanding its structure prepares you to follow the detailed arguments that come later.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Understanding the Index of Jadal Issues
Lists fiqhi issues debated dialectically and an index of scholars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the structure and purpose of a jadal index in usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Jadal indexes map the battlefield of fiqhi debates.

This passage from 'Jadal Usuliyyin' presents a list of fiqhi issues that were debated using dialectical reasoning (jadal). Each issue is accompanied by page numbers, guiding readers to the relevant discussions. Understanding how to navigate such indexes is essential for efficiently accessing scholarly debates on specific topics.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the list format
Observe that the passage on page 538 lists fiqhi issues in a bullet-like structure. Each line begins with a topic (e.g., 'Killing a Muslim for an unbeliever') followed by page numbers. This is not continuous prose but a navigational tool.
The numbers refer to pages in the larger work.
2
Identify the common thread
Note that all listed issues are topics of debate. They involve rulings on homicide, expiation, prayer, theft, and others. This shows the range of fiqh subjects addressed through jadal.
Jadal here means dialectical reasoning, distinct from general logic.
3
Connect to the discipline of jadal
Understand that this index is specific to the book 'Jadal Usuliyyin', which applies jadal to usul al-fiqh. The page numbers allow readers to locate the actual arguments for each issue.
The index assumes familiarity with jadal methodology.
4
Use the index for study
Pick one issue, such as 'Expiation: is it obligatory for intentional murder?' and find its page numbers. This trains you to retrieve targeted information from a scholarly work.
This skill is valuable for research and debate preparation.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Navigating the Biographical Index (Fihris al-A'lam)
Lists fiqhi issues debated dialectically and an index of scholars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to locate scholars in a fihris al-a'lam and understand its role in scholarly works.

Core Idea
A fihris al-a'lam is a scholarly compass.

The second part of the passage presents a 'Fihris al-A'lam' (Index of Notables), listing names of scholars and figures referenced in the book. This index is a standard feature in Islamic scholarly works, allowing readers to quickly find biographical references. Learning to navigate such indexes is crucial for contextualizing arguments and identifying the authorities behind them.

Guided Path
1
Locate the section heading
Find the phrase 'ثامنا : فهرس الأعلام' (Eighth: Index of Notables) in the Arabic. This marks the beginning of the biographical list.
The word 'ثامنا' indicates this is the eighth section of the book's back matter.
2
Scan the entry format
Notice that each entry starts with a dash and then the name, often with a patronymic or nisba (e.g., 'إبراهيم بن إسماعيل بن حبيبة المدني'). Some entries include a brief description like 'الإمام صاحب المذهب' for Ahmad ibn Hanbal.
Names are alphabetized or grouped by first letter, though here it starts with alif.
3
Identify diversity of figures
Observe that the list includes early fuqaha (e.g., Ibrahim al-Nakha'i), founders of schools (Ahmad ibn Hanbal), theologians (al-Ash'ari), and even non-Muslims (Aristotle). This shows the multidisciplinary nature of jadal discussions.
Aristotle's inclusion reflects engagement with Greek logic in Islamic thought.
4
Use the index for research
Pick one name, such as 'الأشعري' (al-Ash'ari), and note his full name as given. Then consider why he might be cited in a work on jadal in usul al-fiqh.
This trains you to connect names to their contributions.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Navigating a Scholarly Bibliography in Jadal and Usul
Lists the references and sources consulted in the book Jadal Usuliyyin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key categories of sources in a jadal/usul bibliography and assess their relevance to Islamic argumentation studies.

Core Idea
A scholarly bibliography is a map of the tradition's intellectual resources.

A bibliography like the one in 'Jadal Usuliyyin' is not just a list—it is a curated selection of works that shape the field. This lesson will help you understand how to read such a bibliography, recognize the types of sources (classical usul, jadal manuals, contemporary studies), and use it to locate authoritative references for your own research in Islamic argumentation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the discipline of each source
Scan the titles and authors. Note works on usul al-fiqh (e.g., al-Shawkani, al-Sarakhsi), jadal (e.g., Ibn al-Hanbali's 'Extraction of debate'), and ethics (e.g., al-Maidani). This reveals the interdisciplinary nature of the field.
Works like 'Al-Irshad' by al-Juwayni and 'Al-Bahr al-Muhit' are major usul texts.
2
Note the author's scholarly lineage and period
Check publication dates and editors. Classical authors (e.g., al-Shafi'i, Ibn Qayyim) versus modern scholars (e.g., al-Qaradawi, al-Zuhayli) show the continuity of the tradition.
The range from 2nd century AH (al-Shafi'i) to 15th century AH (al-Zuhayli) demonstrates living scholarship.
3
Determine relevance to jadal and usul
Look for terms like 'jadal', 'munazarah', 'adab al-bahth', or 'qawa'id usuliyyah'. The bibliography includes works directly on debate (e.g., #12, #17) and foundational usul texts that inform debate methodology.
Ibn Qayyim's 'I'lam al-Muwaqqi'in' and al-Shawkani's 'Irshad al-Fuhul' are key for argumentation theory.
4
Evaluate completeness for research
Assess whether the bibliography covers different schools (Hanafi, Shafi‘i, Maliki, Hanbali) and genres (printed books, editions, contemporary studies). Notice gaps if any.
This list includes both classical and modern sources, but you may need to supplement with works on specific debates.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography listing the primary and secondary sources consulted in the book 'Jadal Usuliyyin'. It contains 24 entries (numbered 11-34 from the list) covering works on Islamic logic, argumentation, usul al-fiqh, and related fields. The list includes classical works like al-Shawkani's 'Irshad al-Fuhul', al-Juwayni's 'al-Irshad', and Ibn Qayyim's 'I'lam al-Muwaqqi'in', as well as modern studies. The bibliography demonstrates the interdisciplinary nature of the book, drawing from Quranic sciences, hadith, logic, and legal theory. Each entry provides author, title, editor, publisher, and date, showing the scholarly rigor. The focus is on sources relevant to jadal (debate) and usul (principles).

أصول الفقه

Key Takeaway
A scholarly bibliography in jadal and usul is a curated guide to the authoritative voices and resources that shape Islamic argumentation theory.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Select any two sources from the list—one classical and one modern—and compare their roles in the study of jadal. How does the classical work (e.g., #17) differ in purpose from the modern one (e.g., #13)?

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Navigating a Bibliography of Jadal and Usul al-Fiqh Sources
Bibliography listing references for Jadal Usuliyyin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key components of a scholarly bibliography in jadal usuliyyin and extract publication information from entries 24–47.

Core Idea
A bibliography reveals the scholarly ecosystem behind a work.

This passage lists the references used in Jadal Usuliyyin. It shows the range of sources, from classical usul al-fiqh works like al-Burhan to modern studies. Understanding how to read a bibliography is essential for any researcher tracing the development of Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify entry structure
Each entry provides author, title, editor (if any), edition, publisher, and date. Entries 24–47 follow this pattern consistently.
For example, entry 34: al-Bahr al-Muhit by al-Zarkashi, edited by a group of scholars, 2nd ed., Kuwait Ministry of Awqaf, 1413 H.
2
Categorize by discipline
Sort works into usul al-fiqh, language, history, and biography. For instance, entries 34 and 37 are usul al-fiqh; entries 39 and 40 are language and history.
This helps understand the breadth of sources used in jadal research.
3
Assess geographical and temporal scope
Note the publishers: Beirut, Cairo, Kuwait, India. Authors span from the 8th to 20th centuries (e.g., al-Shafi'i d. 204 H to al-Zuhayli d. contemporary).
This shows the global and historical reach of the discipline.
4
Identify foundational works
Look for works cited repeatedly in jadal studies, like al-Burhan by al-Juwayni (entry 37). Such works are essential references.
Recognizing key texts helps prioritize reading.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
How to Use a Bibliography in Islamic Scholarship
Author lists bibliographic references for the study.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key components of a bibliographic entry and evaluate its usefulness for research in Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
A bibliography is the backbone of scholarly accountability.

A bibliography is more than a list; it is a scholarly apparatus that allows the reader to trace the sources used by the author. In Islamic intellectual tradition, precise citation is critical for verifying hadith, usul, and tafsir. This lesson will guide you through reading the bibliography from the book 'Jadal Usuliyyin' and understanding how each entry serves the broader scholarly project.

Guided Path
1
Identify the title and author
For each entry, locate the full title of the work and the author's name. Note the author's death date (if given), which helps place the work historically.
The death date is often given in Hijri, e.g., 'ت: 682 هـ'.
2
Note editorial and publication details
See who edited or verified the text, the publisher, edition number, and date. These details indicate the reliability and accessibility of the source.
A critical edition (تحقيق) is more reliable than an unedited reprint.
3
Classify the work by discipline
Determine if the work is in tafsir, hadith, usul al-fiqh, etc. This classification shows the breadth of sources used in a jadal study.
For example, entry #56 is Tafsir al-Baghawi (tafsir), while #60 is Al-Talkhis fi Usul al-Fiqh (usul).
4
Assess the source's significance
Consider why the author included this source. Is it a primary or secondary source? Does it represent a particular school or methodology?
Primary sources like early usul works are foundational; secondary sources like modern studies provide context.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography (list of references) from the book 'Jadal Usuliyyin'. It is not a logical argument or definition, but rather a front matter listing the sources consulted or cited in the work. The list includes classical and modern works in tafsir, hadith, usul al-fiqh, and other Islamic sciences. Each entry provides the author, title, editor, publisher, and date when available. This bibliography serves as a scholarly apparatus showing the breadth of references used by the author of 'Jadal Usuliyyin'. It is typical in academic works to include such a list to document sources. The entries are numbered from 48 to 69, indicating that this is a continuation of a larger bibliography. The titles cover a range of Islamic disciplines, reflecting the interdisciplinary nature of jadal (dialectic) studies. As this is purely a reference list, there is no logical operation to parse; the student should recognize it as a research tool.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Navigating an Islamic Bibliography of Usul and Jadal
Author lists sources and references for the study of Jadal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to parse a bibliographic entry from an Islamic scholarly work and identify its key components (author, title, editor, publisher, date).

Core Idea
Bibliographies are roadmaps to the scholarly tradition – learn to read them.

This passage is a bibliography of sources cited in 'Jadal Usuliyyin', a work on the principles of dialectical theology (jadal). As a student of Islamic logic, you will encounter such lists frequently. They are not mere formalities; they are essential for tracing the transmission of ideas and verifying the authority of arguments. In this lesson, we will dissect one entry to understand its structure and significance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the entry numbering
Each entry begins with a number (e.g., 91, 92). This is a standard way to organize a list. Notice that the numbers are sequential, indicating the order of references.
The numbering helps in cross-referencing within the text.
2
Extract the title and author
The title of the work is given first (e.g., 'شرح تنقيح الفصول'), followed by the author's full name and death date in parentheses. The author's name is crucial for knowing who wrote the work.
The death date (e.g., ت 684هـ) helps place the author in historical context.
3
Note the editorial information
After the author, there is often 'تحقيق' (tahqiq) indicating the editor of the edition. The editor's name and publication details (publisher, place, edition number, date) follow.
Editions vary; the editor and publisher ensure you are looking at a reliable version.
4
Classify the work by subject
Most entries are on usul al-fiqh (principles of jurisprudence), but some are on language (e.g., al-Sihah) or history (e.g., Tabaqat). Recognizing the subject helps you understand the breadth of sources used.
This bibliography shows that jadal draws from multiple disciplines.

Source pages p. 563

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography of sources that the author of 'Jadal Usuliyyin' has consulted or referenced. It lists works from various Islamic sciences, primarily usul al-fiqh (principles of jurisprudence), but also language, logic, and history. The entries include commentaries on classical texts, such as Sharh Tanqih al-Fusul by al-Qarafi and Sharh al-Kawkab al-Munir by Ibn al-Najjar, as well as independent works like al-Ghazali's Shifa' al-Ghalil and al-Tufi's 'Ilm al-Jadhal. The bibliography is arranged numerically, with each entry containing the title, author, editor, publisher, and date. This list serves as a reference for scholars and students of usul al-fiqh and jadal (dialectical theology). It is typical of the academic tradition to include such a bibliography to establish the authority and breadth of sources used.

Checkpoint
Which of the following works is included in this bibliography?
A) Sharh al-Mukhtasar by Ibn al-Hajib
B) al-Ahkam fi Usul al-Ahkam by al-Amidi
C) Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya al-Kubra by al-Subki
D) al-Burhan fi Wujuh al-Bayan by Ibn Wahb

Key Takeaway
An Islamic bibliography is not a dry list; it is a curated map of the sources that underpin the author's argument, and learning to read it is essential for rigorous scholarship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Select one entry from the list (e.g., entry 91) and write a one-sentence summary of the work's subject matter and significance for usul al-fiqh.
?
Identify three entries that are commentaries (sharh) on earlier texts. List their numbers and the original texts they explain.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
10 min
Reading a Bibliography in Islamic Logic
List of bibliographical sources used in the work.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to categorize bibliographical entries from an Islamic logic work by subject and assess their relevance to the study of jadal and usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
A bibliography is not a list—it is a map of the intellectual tradition that fed the author's argument.

This passage may look like a dry list of books, but it is a goldmine. It tells you exactly which works the author relied on for his arguments in jadal (dialectics) and usul al-fiqh (legal theory). By learning to read a bibliography, you can trace the author's chain of authority and verify his sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Subject Categories
Scan the entries and group them by subject: lexicons (e.g., Mu'jam al-Kabir, Mu'jam Mufradat), works on jadal (e.g., Al-Ma'unah fi al-Jadal, Al-Minhaj fi Tartib al-Hijaj), works on usul al-fiqh (e.g., Al-Mughni fi Usul al-Fiqh, Muntaha al-Wusul), and general works (e.g., Muqaddimat Ibn Khaldun).
2
Note Author and Era
For each entry, observe the author's name and death date. This tells you the chronological depth of the author's sources. For example, al-Tabarani (d. 360 AH) and al-Shirazi (d. 476 AH) span centuries.
The author used both early and later sources to build a comprehensive argument.
3
Compare Multiple Editions
Notice that some works appear with different editors or publishers (e.g., Mu'jam Mufradat Alfaz al-Qur'an appears twice). This indicates the popularity and textual history of the work.
Multiple editions may reflect revisions or different manuscript traditions.
4
Connect to the Main Text's Arguments
As you read the main text of Jadal Usuliyyin, refer back to this bibliography to see which sources are cited. For instance, if the author discusses the rules of debate, check if he relies on al-Shirazi's Al-Ma'unah fi al-Jadal or al-Baji's Al-Minhaj.
This helps you evaluate the authority and originality of the author's claims.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography section listing the sources used by the author of Jadal Usuliyyin. It covers entries 145 to 167, each referencing classical works in Islamic sciences such as lexicons (mu'jams), works on logic and dialectic (jadal), jurisprudence (usul al-fiqh), and related fields. The list includes well-known authors like al-Tabarani, al-Raghib al-Isfahani, al-Shirazi, al-Sakkaki, Ibn Khaldun, Ibn al-Hajib, al-Ghazali, and al-Baydawi. The entries provide detailed publication information including editors, publishers, and dates. This section serves as a scholarly apparatus, allowing the reader to verify and consult the original sources referenced in the main text.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Navigating Jadal Usuliyyin: The Book's Grand Outline
Table of contents outlining the book's structure from introductory chapter to first two chapters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the two-part structure of Jadal Usuliyyin and identify the key topics covered in each section.

Core Idea
Jadal is a universal human phenomenon rooted in revelation and tradition.

This lesson introduces the table of contents of Jadal Usuliyyin, a comprehensive work on dialectical argumentation (jadal) in the context of usul al-fiqh. By understanding the book's structure, you will see how the author systematically traces jadal from its innate human origins through its manifestation in the Quran and Sunnah, to its development among early scholars and its formalization by Imam al-Shafi'i. This roadmap will help you follow the argumentative flow of the entire work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main sections
Look at the table of contents after the introduction. It begins with a preliminary chapter (الباب التمهيدي) and then a second section (الفصل الثاني). Note their titles: the first covers roots and early development, the second covers origin and development of jadal research among usuliyyin.
2
Examine the first section's subsections
The preliminary chapter has two sections, each with multiple subsections. Trace the flow from jadal as innate disposition (المبحث الأول), to Quranic jadal (المبحث الثاني), Sunnah (المبحث الثالث), companions/followers (المبحث الرابع), and mujtahid imams (المبحث الخامس). This shows the progression from universal to Islamic sources to historical eras.
3
Examine the second section's focus
The second section has two subsections: the stage of origin (focus on Imam al-Shafi'i and his works) and the stage of development and integration. This reveals the book's historical approach to jadal as a theoretical discipline.
4
Connect the structure to the author's thesis
The author argues that jadal is not an imported Greek method but has Islamic roots. The table of contents supports this by starting with innate human disposition and revelation, then tracing historical development through the Shafi'i school.

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents of Jadal Usuliyyin, showing the book's structure. It begins with an introduction and then a preliminary chapter on the roots of jadal and its origin and development among usuliyyin. The first section covers jadal before the science of usul al-fiqh, examining it as an innate human disposition, in the Quran, in the Sunnah, among the Companions and Followers, and in the era of mujtahid imams. The second section discusses the origin and development of jadal research among usuliyyin, starting with the stage of origin and establishment focusing on Imam al-Shafi'i, his works, and later developments, followed by a stage of development and integration. The table of contents provides a roadmap for the book's systematic treatment of jadal in Islamic legal theory.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
10 min
Navigating the Structure of Jadal Usuliyyin
Lists the chapters and sections of the book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to parse the table of contents of Jadal Usuliyyin and identify the logical progression from historical roots to theoretical analysis.

Core Idea
A table of contents is a logical map: it reveals the author's argumentative structure before you read a single line.

The table of contents (fihris) is not just a list of pages—it is a blueprint of the author's thought process. In Jadal Usuliyyin, the arrangement of chapters and sections reflects a deliberate movement from the historical emergence of dialectic among usulis to its theoretical foundations. By learning to read this map, you will gain a bird's-eye view of how the author builds his case, which will help you orient yourself when studying the full text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the major divisions
Look at the highest-level headings: 'Preliminary Section' (الباب التمهيدي), 'Part One' (الباب الأول), and within them, the chapters and sections. Notice that the book is split into a historical part (roots and development) and a theoretical part (concept and method).
The preliminary section covers history; Part One covers theory.
2
Trace the historical timeline
In the preliminary section, follow the subsections: they move from dialectic in the Quran to the Sunnah, then Companions, Followers, and finally the era of the independent imams. This chronological order shows the author's attempt to ground usuli dialectic in scripture and early practice.
The timeline culminates in the formation of madhhabs and the intensification of usuli debate.
3
Observe the theoretical architecture
Part One begins with a chapter on the concept of dialectic, then moves to the foundations of its method: rational reflection, definition, and inference. This sequence mirrors the logical order of any systematic inquiry: first define your subject, then establish its tools, then apply them.
Notice that 'inference' (الاستدلال) comes after definition, showing the author's emphasis on proper groundwork.
4
Link the parts to the author's argument
Ask yourself: why does the author start with history? Because he wants to show that dialectic is not a foreign innovation but a legitimate discipline rooted in revelation and early Islamic scholarship. The theoretical part then provides the rules for using dialectic correctly. This structure itself is an argument for the validity and necessity of usuli dialectic.
The table of contents is thus a condensed version of the book's thesis.

It provides a comprehensive outline of the book's structure, divided into preliminary sections, chapters, and subsections. The book is organized into two main parts: the first part covers the roots, origin, and development of dialectic (jadal) among the usulis (scholars of usul al-fiqh), including its presence in the Quran, Sunnah, and early Islamic periods. The second part addresses the theory of dialectic among the usulis, including the concept of jadal, its foundations, and the methods of definition and inference. The table of contents serves as a roadmap for the reader, showing the logical progression from historical background to theoretical analysis.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Navigating the Book's Structure via its Table of Contents
Structural outline of a book on juridical dialectic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to parse the table of contents of a scholarly work to identify its two main parts, chapters, and subsections.

Core Idea
A table of contents is a structural map; mastering it unlocks the author's argument.

This lesson helps you read a table of contents as a logical outline. The TOC of 'Jadal Usuliyyin' reveals the author's plan: first theory, then applications. You will learn to trace the flow from linguistic foundations to practical objections in scriptural inference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main parts
Note that the book is divided into Part One (Theory) and Part Two (Applications). This is the highest-level structure.
Part One covers conceptual foundations; Part Two shows dialectic in action.
2
Examine the chapters in Part One
Part One has four chapters: Concept, Foundations, Elements, Etiquettes. Each chapter builds on the previous.
Pay attention to the progression from definition to method to rules.
3
Break down a chapter into sections and subsections
For example, Chapter One has four sections; each section has subsections (matalib). This shows granular detail.
The numbering (مبحث، مطلب) indicates hierarchy.
4
Locate the applications in Part Two
Part Two focuses on dialectic in inference from the Quran. Notice the types of objections listed.
This part is more specific and shows the practical use of the theory.

Commentary
This passage is a table of contents for the book 'Jadal Usuliyyin' (Juridical Dialectic). It presents the overall structure of the work in two main parts. Part One covers the theory of dialectic among the jurists, including its concept, foundations, method elements, and etiquettes. Part Two deals with applications of dialectic, specifically in inference from the Quran. The table shows a detailed breakdown into chapters, sections, and subsections. The student should use this as a roadmap for the book's contents. The early sections cover linguistic and terminological definitions, then move to the foundations of rational reflection, definition, and inference. Later sections address the question-and-answer structure and etiquettes. The applications part focuses on objections related to scriptural evidence.

Key Terms
الجدل (al-jadal): dialectic
الأصوليون (al-usuliyyun): jurists of usul
المناظرة (al-munazara): debate
الخلاف (al-khilaf): disagreement

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Chapter One of Part Two
D) Chapter Three of Part One

Key Takeaway
A table of contents reveals the author's logical structure; parsing it prepares you to follow the argument from theory to application.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the table of contents, list the three types of objections discussed in Part Two, Chapter One, Section Two.
?
Trace the argument of Part One by writing a one-paragraph summary of how the chapters build on each other, based only on the TOC headings.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Navigating the Structure of Jadal Usuliyyin
Table of contents listing chapters and sections on jadal in usul al-fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the main parts, chapters, and sections of the book 'Jadal Usuliyyin' and the key topics covered in Usuli jadal.

Core Idea
A table of contents is a roadmap to the arguments in Usuli jadal.

This lesson helps you orient yourself in the book by mapping its structure. The table of contents reveals how the author organizes his treatment of dialectical inference in usul al-fiqh: from the importance of inference and types of evidence, to the method and etiquettes of jadal, and finally to applications in inference by the Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main parts
Scan the TOC for major divisions. The text is divided into two major parts: the first covers theoretical foundations and etiquettes, the second covers practical applications.
Look for 'الباب الأول' and 'الباب الثاني'.
2
List the chapters under each part
Under Part One, find chapters on importance of inference, textual and rational evidences, method of jadal, and etiquettes. Under Part Two, chapters on inference by the Book and by the Sunnah.
3
Recognize the sections and demands
Each chapter contains sections (مبحث) and demands (مطلب). Notice the hierarchy: chapter -> section -> demand. This shows the granularity of topics.
For example, Chapter 1 of Part Two has sections on various types of objections.
4
Note the key objections discussed
Focus on the categories of objections to inference by the Book and Sunnah: e.g., objection by not adhering to the evidence, by accepting implication, by claiming participation, by differences in readings, by abrogation, by interpretation, and by counterevidence.
This list is a checklist for Usuli jadal.

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents of the book 'Jadal Usuliyyin'. It outlines the structure of the work, which is divided into parts, chapters, sections, and demands. The first part covers the importance of inference in Usuli dialectic, textual and rational evidences, and the elements of the dialectical method according to the Usulis. It then details etiquettes of dialectic related to personality, relationship, subject, and style. The second part applies dialectic to inference by the Quran, covering various objections such as not adhering to the evidence, accepting the implication, participation in evidence, differences in readings, abrogation, interpretation, and counterevidence. It then similarly treats inference by the Sunnah, including objections related to chain of transmission, text, and cause. The page numbers interspersed indicate where each section begins in the original text.

Key Terms
جدل
الاستدلال
أصولي

Key Takeaway
The structure of Jadal Usuliyyin is a systematic guide to the types of objections and methods in Usuli dialectical reasoning.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Overview of the Book's Subject and Structure
Lists the book's sections on dialectical objections to legal evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the main types of legal evidence discussed in Jadal Usuliyyin and the structure of objections presented in its table of contents.

Core Idea
The table of contents reveals that jadal in usul al-fiqh systematically categorizes objections to every type of legal evidence.

The table of contents of Jadal Usuliyyin is not just a list; it is a roadmap of dialectical method. By parsing its structure, you will see how jurists anticipated and countered objections to legal inferences from the Prophet's actions, analogy, consensus, and more. This overview equips you to navigate the book and understand the breadth of jadal in Islamic legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main chapters
Scan the TOC for the major divisions (chapters). Note the page numbers. The book has four chapters after the introductory sections: Chapter 2 on objections to the Prophet's actions, Chapter 3 on objections to analogy, Chapter 4 on objections to other evidences (consensus, companion's statement, etc.), and a conclusion.
The chapter on analogy is the longest, indicating its central importance.
2
Observe the order of evidence
The book begins with objections to the Prophet's actions, then analogy, then other evidences. Why this order? The Prophet's actions are a primary source; analogy is a secondary source; the other evidences are tertiary. The order reflects descending strength of evidence.
The placement of consensus after analogy is noteworthy; typically, consensus is considered stronger than analogy.
3
Note the types of objections
Under each chapter, see the demands (matālib) that specify particular objections, e.g., 'objection by claiming ambiguity' or 'objection by counterexample'. Each demand is a specific type of critique.
These categories show the systematic nature of jadal: objections are not random but follow a taxonomy.

Source pages p. 576

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents of the book 'Jadal Usuliyyin'. It systematically lists the chapters and sections, showing the work's focus on dialectical objections to various types of legal evidence. The structure begins with objections to the Prophet's actions (af'al), then proceeds to analogy (qiyas), including objections to its authority, pillars, and types of causes. It then covers objections to other evidences such as consensus (ijma'), the Companion's statement (qawl al-sahabi), presumption of continuity (istishab), implication of address (fahwa al-khitab), and explicit address (dalil al-khitab). The index provides page numbers for each section, indicating the detailed treatment of each topic. This listing reveals the book's comprehensive approach to jadal in usul al-fiqh, focusing on refuting arguments against the use of these evidences.

Key Terms
الجدل
الاعتراض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a main chapter in this TOC?
A) Objections to inference by analogy
B) Dialectics in inference by consensus
C) Objections to inference by the Prophet's actions
D) Objections to inference by linguistic analysis

Key Takeaway
The table of contents demonstrates that jadal in usul al-fiqh is a comprehensive discipline that systematically addresses challenges to every type of legal evidence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify under which chapter of this TOC an objection to the Prophet's act by claiming abrogation (naskh) would fall. (Answer: Chapter 2, Section 6)
?
Name two types of objections that can be raised against a causal inference (qiyas) according to this TOC.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Objections to the Prophet's Actions
Lists the book's sections on dialectical objections to legal evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and categorize the eight types of objections to inference from the Prophet's actions as outlined in the table of contents.

Core Idea
Every possible flaw in using a prophetic action as evidence is catalogued in eight specific objections.

The second chapter of Jadal Usuliyyin dedicates a section to objections against istidlal bi-af'al al-nabi. The eight 'demands' (matālib) cover everything from the inferrer not acting on it to claims of abrogation. Understanding these categories equips you to evaluate prophetic evidence systematically.

Guided Path
1
Count the demands
The TOC lists 8 demands under 'Fourth investigation: Objections to inference by the actions of the Prophet'. List them. They are numbered from first to eighth.
The page numbers show the relative length of each section; longer sections may indicate more complex debates.
2
Categorize by type
Some objections challenge the inference itself (e.g., disagreement in implication), some challenge the reliability (e.g., difference in narration), some challenge the authority (e.g., claim of abrogation). Group them into these three categories.
This classification helps in memorizing and applying the objections.
3
Note the page numbers
The page numbers show the relative depth of treatment. The longest section might be the most debated. For instance, the second demand (disputing implication) spans 3 pages, while the first demand (inferrer does not act) spans 1 page.
This indicates which objections were considered most significant by the author.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
7 min
Objections to Analogy (Qiyas)
Lists the book's sections on dialectical objections to legal evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three main categories of objections to qiyas and name specific sub-objections for each.

Core Idea
Objections to analogy are divided by whether they attack its authority, its structural pillars, or the cause (illa) itself.

The longest section of the TOC deals with objections to qiyas. It is subdivided into investigations on authority (hujjiyya), pillars (arkan), the effective cause, the correlational cause, and various specific objections. This hierarchy shows the complexity of defending analogical reasoning. Understanding this structure allows you to quickly locate the relevant counterargument in a debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main investigations
Look at the TOC under 'Third chapter: Dialectics in inference by analogy'. Find the four investigations: (1) from the angle of authority, (2) on the general pillars of analogy, (3) on the effective cause, (4) on the correlational cause.
Each investigation groups related types of objections.
2
List the demands under each investigation
For example, under the first investigation there are eight demands about the authority of qiyas in different domains (principles, names, customs, etc.). Under the second investigation there are five demands challenging the pillars (asl, hukm, illa, etc.).
Note the page numbers: longer lists indicate more sub-issues.
3
Distinguish between effective cause and correlational cause
The effective cause (al-illa al-mu'aththira) objections include requests for correction, inefficacy, counterargument, and inversion. The correlational cause (al-illa al-tardiyya) objections include corruption of presupposition, counterexample, splitting, etc. Understand the difference: effective cause is proven by the mujtahid; correlational cause is a formal condition.
This distinction is crucial in usul al-fiqh debates.

Navigating the Apparatus of a Scholarly Work
Table of contents listing the book's conclusion, indexes, and subject index.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to locate and distinguish the ten general indexes in the book 'Jadal Usuliyyin' and explain the purpose of each.

Core Idea
Indexes are scholarly compasses for navigating primary sources.

This table of contents reveals the end-matter of a substantive work in usul al-fiqh. Understanding what each index contains is essential for efficient research — you need to know where to find Quranic verses, hadiths, narrations, usuli rules, and notable figures. Let's parse the list systematically.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Major Sections
Notice the three main parts: 'Results of the research and its horizons', 'Conclusion', and 'General indexes'. The indexes are then numbered from one to ten, plus a subject index.
2
Classify the Indexes by Content Type
Group them: textual sources (Quran verses, hadiths, narrations, poems), conceptual tools (terms, usuli rules, fiqh rulings), and bibliographic aids (notable figures, books mentioned, sources and references).
3
Map Each Index to a Research Need
For each index, ask: What would I use this for? For example, 'Index of Quranic verses' helps locate where a specific verse is discussed. 'Index of usuli rules' helps find discussions of legal maxims.
4
Recognize the Subject Index's Role
The final 'Subject index' is thematic — it covers concepts and topics not captured by the specialized indexes. It is often the broadest search tool.

Introducing 'Al-Jadal 'inda al-Usuliyyin'
Title page of a modern academic work.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the scope and significance of the book 'Al-Jadal 'inda al-Usuliyyin' within the Islamic legal theory tradition.

Core Idea
This work connects classical jadal theory with practical usul al-fiqh reasoning.

This lesson orients you to a modern academic work that studies dialectic (jadal) as practiced by Islamic jurists (usuliyyun). The title page tells us the book is part of a university series and authored by a contemporary scholar. Understanding the context of this work helps situate the classical jadal texts you will study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work and series
Look at the title: 'Al-Jadal 'inda al-Usuliyyin: Between Theory and Practice'. It is number 109 in the Al-Rushd Series of University Messages. This indicates it is a contemporary academic publication.
The series focuses on university-level research.
2
Note the author's background
The author, Mas'ud ibn Musa al-Falusi, is a lecturer at the Faculty of Islamic Social Sciences, University of Batna, Algeria. His academic position suggests the book is a scholarly study blending Islamic sciences and social sciences.
3
Understand the significance of 'jadal' in usul al-fiqh
Jadal (dialectic) is a method of argumentation used by jurists to defend or refute legal opinions. This book likely examines how jadal was applied in classical usul al-fiqh debates, bridging theory and practice.

Introducing Jadal Among the Legal Theorists
Title page of the book stating the subject and author.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the subject matter and scope of the book 'Al-Jadal inda al-Usuliyyin' based on its title page.

Core Idea
This book connects the theory of dialectic to its practice among Islamic legal theorists.

This lesson is based on the title page of the book 'Al-Jadal inda al-Usuliyyin' (Dialectic Among the Legal Theorists). Although a title page may seem simple, it sets the stage for understanding how jadal (dialectic) is studied in uṣūl al-fiqh. The subtitle 'Between Theory and Practice' indicates that the author aims to examine both the principles and the real-world application of jadal in juristic debates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
The title 'Al-Jadal inda al-Usuliyyin' tells us the book is about jadal (dialectic) as practiced by legal theorists (usuliyyun). Note that the focus is not on general logic but on its use in Islamic jurisprudence.
2
Understand the subtitle
The subtitle 'Between Theory and Practice' suggests the book will cover both the theoretical framework of jadal and its application in actual debates among usuliyyun.
3
Recognize the author and context
The author, Dr. Masoud bin Musa Falousi, is a lecturer at the University of Batna, Algeria. This indicates an academic, contemporary study of classical jadal methods.
4
Set expectations for content
Given the title and subtitle, we can expect discussions on the rules of jadal, examples from usul al-fiqh debates, and how theory informs practice. This is not a general logic book but a specialized work on juristic dialectic.

الجَدَلُ عِنْدَ الأُصُولِيِّينَ بَيْنَ النَّظَرِيَّةِ وَالتَّطْبِيقِ

مكتبة الرشد
Dialectic Among the Legal Theorists: Between Theory and Practice. Written by Dr. Masoud bin Musa Falousi, Lecturer in the Faculty of Islamic Sciences, University of Batna - Algeria. Al-Rushd Publishers.
Source pages p. 581

Commentary
This passage is the title page of the book. It identifies the subject as 'Al-Jadal inda al-Usuliyyin' (Dialectic Among the Legal Theorists), with the subtitle 'Between Theory and Practice.' The author is Dr. Masoud bin Musa Falousi, a lecturer at the University of Batna, Algeria. This indicates that the book will discuss the logical art of dialectic (jadal) as employed by scholars of uṣūl al-fiqh, examining both theoretical principles and practical applications.
